ويلزم بإيجاب وقبول وضعا للمضي، وبتعاط
سمي
ويلزم بإيجاب وقبول أي ينعقد البيع انعقاداً لازماً، الانعقاد: عبارة عن انضمام كلام أحد المتعاقدين إلى الآخر على وجه يظهر أثره في المحل شرعا، أي الأثر الشرعي بالبيع يظهر في المحل عند الإيجاب والقبول، حتى يكون العاقد قادراً على التصرف والإيجاب ما يتلفظ به أولاً سواء كان من جانب البائع أو المشتري، وإنما إيجاباً؛ لأنه أوجب أي أثبت جواباً على صاحبه (كفاية، فتح بإيجاب: [خرج بيع المكروه؛ إذ الغرض بيان بيع النافذ. (ملا إلياس وهو عبارة عما يتقدم من أحد المتعاقدين من قولهما بعت واشتريت، وظهر منه أن القبول عبارة عما يتأخر منهما. (كفاية)
من
وضعا للمضي: [ أي بصيغة الماضي فلا ينعقد إذا كان أحدهما مستقبلا. (چلپی)] أي يلزم العقد إذا كان الإيجاب والقبول بصيغة الماضي كقول البائع: "بعت"، والمشتري: "اشتريت"؛ لأن الشرع يعتبر الإخبار إنشاء في جميع العقود، فينعقد به، ومقتضاه أنه لا ينعقد بحال وليس كذلك، بل ينعقد بلفظين ينبئان عن التمليك والتملك على صيغة الماضي أو الحال لكن ينعقد في الحال بالنية في الأصح. فإن قيل: النية إنما تعمل في المحتملات لا في الموضوعات الأصلية، والمضارع عند الفقهاء حقيقة في الحال فلا يحتاج إلى النية. قلنا: إن كونه حقيقة في الحال مختصة بغير البيوع، والحقيقة الشرعية فيها هو لفظ الماضي؛ لأن النبي عليه استعمل فيه لفظ الماضي الذي يدل على تحقق وجوده، والمضارع فيها مجاز يحتاج إلى النية، وهذا في ما يحتمل الحال والاستقبال أما ما تمحض للحال كـ أبيعك الآن" فلا يحتاج إلى النية، وأما ما تمحض للاستقبال المقرون بالسين أو سوف أو الأمر فلا ينعقد به؛ لأن لفظ المستقبل إن كان جانب البائع كان وعدا وإن كان من جانب المشتري كان مساومة وطلباً لا إيجاباً، ولما لزم العقد بإيجاب وقبول بصيغة الماضي فلا خيار لواحد منهما إلا بعيب أو بعدم رؤية وقال الشافعي: لا يلزم العقد بالإيجاب والقبول بل للعاقدين الخيار في المجلس، يرد العقد بدون رضاء صاحبه؛ لقوله علي: "المتبايعان بالخيار ما لم يتفرقا"، وبه قال أحمد. ولنا: أن العقد قد تم من الجانبين، ودخل المبيع في ملك المشتري، وإثبات الخيار لأحدهما يستلزم إبطال حق الآخر، فينتفي؛ لقوله علي : " لا ضرر ولا ضرار في الإسلام والحديث محمول على خيار القبول، فإنه إذا أوجب أحدهما، فلكل منهما الخيار ما داما في المجلس، ولم يأخذا في عمل آخر، وفي لفظ الحديث إشارة إليه، فإنهما متبايعان حالة البيع حقيقة، وما بعده أو قبله مجازاً كسائر أسماء الفاعلين مثل المتجاذبين والمتضاربين، فيكون التفرق على هذا بالأقوال، هذا تأويل محمد، وقال أبو يوسف هو التفرق بالأبدان بعد الإيجاب قبل القبول. [رمز الحقائق: ٣/٢] (فتح، عناية) وبتعاط: أي ويلزم البيع أيضاً بتناول مطلقاً سواء كان خسيساً أو نفيساً في الأصح، وعن الكرخي جواز ذلك في الخسائس دون النفائس وهو قول أحمد وعند الشافعي: لا ينعقد البيع بالتعاطي مطلقاً؛ لأن الإيجاب والقبول من أركان البيع، قلنا: جواز العقد باعتبار الرضا لا بصورة ،اللفظ، وقد وجد التراضي في التعاطي، -
The book of sales. What pertains to the sale. It becomes binding by offer and acceptance in the past tense, and by mutual delivery. 'It becomes binding by offer and acceptance' meaning the sale becomes a binding contract. 'In the past tense' meaning with the past tense form, so it does not conclude if one is future. The contract becomes binding when the offer and acceptance are in the past tense like the seller says 'I sold' and the buyer 'I bought' because the Law considers informing as initiating in all contracts. Al-Shafi'i said: The contract is not binding by offer and acceptance; rather the parties have the option in the session, they can annul without the other's consent due to the hadith 'The two parties in a sale have the option as long as they have not separated'. Our evidence: The contract is complete from both sides, the sold item entered the buyer's ownership, and establishing option for one necessitates nullifying the other's right, which is negated by 'No harm and no reciprocating harm in Islam'. The hadith is interpreted as the option of acceptance. 'And by mutual delivery' meaning the sale also becomes binding by taking hand-to-hand absolutely, whether cheap or precious according to the soundest view. Al-Karkhi said it is permissible only for cheap items, and Ahmad said likewise. Al-Shafi'i said the sale is not valid by mutual delivery at all because offer and acceptance are pillars. We say: The permissibility of the contract is based on consent, not the form of words, and mutual consent is found in mutual delivery.
Source pages p. 250

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with proof regarding the binding nature of a sale. The text from Kanz al-Daqa'iq states that a sale becomes binding (lazim) when there is an offer (ijab) and acceptance (qabul) uttered in the past tense (madi). The commentary explains that the past tense is required because Shariah treats informative statements as performative (insha') in contracts. If the present tense is used, it may still be valid with intention in the soundest view, except when it is purely future (with saufa or amr) where it does not work. The Hanafi position is that once the contract is concluded with past tense, neither party has an option (khiyar) except for defects or non-seeing. The Shafi'i school holds that both parties retain the option (khiyar al-majlis) until they physically separate, citing the hadith 'The two parties have the option as long as they have not separated.' The Hanafi response clarifies that the hadith refers to the option before acceptance (khiyar al-qabul), not after the contract is finalized. Imam Muhammad interprets 'separation' as separation by words, while Abu Yusuf considers it as separation by bodies after the offer and before the acceptance. The second part discusses mutual delivery (ta'ati), where a sale is also binding by hand-to-hand exchange without verbal offer and acceptance. The Hanafi position is that this is valid absolutely, basing the contract on mutual consent (taraadi) rather than verbal form. This is opposed by al-Shafi'i who insists on verbal pillars, and al-Karkhi and Ahmad who limit it to cheap items. The commentary emphasizes that if mutual consent is evident, the contract is binding.

Key Terms
تعاط (ta'āṭī): Hand-to-hand exchange of goods and price without verbal offer and acceptance.
تراضي (tarāḍī): Mutual consent, the basis of contracts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the soundest Hanafi view, a sale by mutual delivery (ta'ati) is:
A) Invalid because no verbal offer and acceptance.
B) Valid only for cheap items.
C) Valid and binding for all items.
D) Valid but not binding until the parties separate.

Key Takeaway
Ta'ati is a valid and binding sale in Hanafi fiqh, based on mutual consent, and applies to all items regardless of value.

Standing Up After Offer Voids the Offer
Explaining that standing up after offer voids the offer before acceptance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on standing up after an offer, identify the exception for khul' and manumission, and explain the Shafi'i difference.

Core Idea
Standing up after an offer cancels the acceptance option, except in khul' and manumission.

In Hanafi law, the acceptance option (khiyar al-qabul) lasts until the end of the session. However, if either party stands up, it is considered evidence of withdrawal, voiding the offer. This lesson explains the reasoning and an exception for personal status contracts.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
Identify the hukm: standing up after offer but before acceptance invalidates the offer. The other party loses the right to accept.
2
Identify the evidence
The commentary gives two proofs: 1) Standing indicates i'rad (turning away) and ruju' (returning), so the offer is void by analogy to other exchange contracts. 2) The Quranic principle 'no hardship' (22:78) supports treating the session as one unit.
3
Note the exception
Khul' (divorce by redemption) and manumission for payment are exceptions because they are considered oaths (yamin) from the initiator, and oaths are not invalidated by standing.
4
Explain the Shafi'i dispute
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that acceptance must be immediate; the session is not a single unit. The Hanafi response argues that this would cause hardship, contrary to the Quran.
5
Apply the ruling
In practice, if a seller says 'I sold' and the buyer stands up, the offer is void. If the buyer later returns, he cannot accept. The session ends when either party stands.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأي قام عن المجلس قبل القبول بطل الإيجاب
وأي قام أي أي واحد من المتعاقدين بطل الإيجاب: [لأن القيام دليل الإعراض والرجوع، فيبطل به كسائر عقود المبادلة، فلا يبقى للآخر ولاية القبول بعده] أي إذا قام أحد المتعاقدين عن المجلس بعد الإيجاب بطل الإيجاب؛ لأن القيام دليل الإعراض والرجوع، فيبطل العقد به كسائر عقود المبادلة بخلاف الخلع والعتق على مال، حيث لا يبطل بقيام الزوج والمولى؛ لأنه يمين من جهتهما والقبول شرط والأيمان لا تبطل بالقيام، وعند الشافعي: خيار القبول لا يمتد إلى آخر المجلس بل هو على الفور، قلنا: إن العاقد يحتاج إلى التردّي والتفكر، فيجعل ساعات المجلس كساعة واحدة وفيما قال الشافعي حرج بين، وهو مدفوع بالنص، قال تعالى: ﴿وَمَا جَعَلَ عَلَيْكُمْ فِي الدِّينِ مِنْ حَرَج ﴾ (الحج:٧٨) [رمز الحقائق: ٣/٢، ٤] (فتح)
'And whoever stands up from the session before acceptance invalidates the offer.' 'Whoever stands up' meaning whichever of the two contracting parties stands up invalidates the offer; because standing is evidence of turning away and returning, so it invalidates the offer like in other exchange contracts. Thus the other party has no authority to accept afterwards. This is unlike khul' and manumission for payment, where standing of the husband or owner does not invalidate because it is an oath from their side and acceptance is a condition, and oaths are not invalidated by standing. According to al-Shafi'i, the option of acceptance does not extend to the end of the session but is immediate. We say: The contracting party needs deliberation and reflection, so the hours of the session are treated as a single hour. What al-Shafi'i said involves hardship, and it is repelled by the text: 'And He has not laid upon you in religion any hardship' (22:78).
Source pages p. 251

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with proof regarding the effect of standing up from the session after the offer but before acceptance. The matn states that if either party stands up, the offer is voided. The commentary explains that standing indicates withdrawal (i'rad) and return (ruju'), so the offer becomes void, similar to other exchange contracts. The other party can no longer accept that offer. An exception is made for khul' and manumission for payment, which are considered oaths (yamin) from the initiating party, and oaths are not invalidated by standing. A dispute with al-Shafi'i is mentioned: he holds that the option of acceptance (khiyar al-qabul) is immediate and does not extend to the end of the session. The Hanafi response argues that the contracting party needs time to deliberate (taraddi and tafakkur), so the entire session is considered like a single hour, and rejecting that would cause hardship, which is contrary to the Quranic principle (22:78).

Key Terms
إعراض (i'rāḍ): Turning away or showing disinterest, which is inferred from standing up.
خيار القبول (khiyār al-qabūl): The period after the offer during which the other party may accept; in Hanafi, it lasts until the end of the session or till one party stands up.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a sale, after the seller makes an offer ('I sold'), the buyer stands up and walks away, then returns and says 'I accept'. According to Hanafi fiqh, is the acceptance valid?
A) Yes, because the offer is still open until the end of the day.
B) Yes, because standing up does not indicate withdrawal.
C) No, because standing up voids the offer.
D) No, because the buyer must accept immediately.

Key Takeaway
Standing up after an offer voids it, except in khul' and manumission, reflecting the Hanafi principle of treating the session as one unit.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
beginner
6 min
Knowledge of Quantity and Description of Price in Sale
Clarifying requirement of knowing quantity and description of price when not pointed.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to STATE the Hanafi condition for knowledge of the countervalues in a sale and APPLY it to distinguish when pointing eliminates the need for description.

Core Idea
A sale is valid only if the price and commodity are known; pointing removes the need for description because it directly removes ignorance.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq and its commentary establishes a key condition for sale contracts: when the price or commodity is not physically indicated, their quantity must be known, and for the price alone, its description (e.g., purity, mint) must also be known. The Hanafi school distinguishes between quantity (required for both) and description (required only for the price), and allows pointing as a practical way to eliminate ignorance. Understanding this ruling protects contracts from gharar (uncertainty) while accommodating common commercial practices.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Matn's Ruling
Read the matn: 'ولا بد من معرفة قدر، ووصف ثمن غير مشار'. Recognize that it imposes a necessity (la budda) to know the quantity (qadr) of both the price and the commodity, and the description (wasf) of the price, when they are not pointed to.
The phrase 'غیر مشار' (ghayr mushar) is key; it applies when the item is not physically indicated.
2
Understand the Exception: Pointed Items
The matn adds 'لا مشار' (la mushar) meaning 'not pointed' — this is the exception. When the countervalues are pointed to (mushar ilayh), the requirement for knowledge of quantity and description drops because the act of pointing eliminates ignorance about identity.
Pointing suffices even if the exact weight or description is unknown.
3
Distinguish Quantity vs. Description
The phrase 'قدر، ووصف ثمن' (qadr, wa wasf thamin) shows that quantity is required for both the thaman (price) and mabī' (commodity), but description (wasf) is explicitly attached to 'thaman' only. Hence, in Hanafi school, description is required only for the price, not the commodity.
This is a distinctive Hanafi rule; other schools may differ.
4
Define Thaman (Price)
The commentary clarifies that 'thaman' here means absolute price (al-thaman al-mutlaq), i.e., dirhams and dinars (silver and gold coins). Other items, such as fungibles or non-fungibles, are considered muthman (commodity) and are subject to different rules.
When currency is exchanged for goods, it always occupies the position of thaman.
5
Apply the Principle
The underlying reason (illah) for the requirement is that ignorance of these essential terms leads to dispute (niza'). Therefore, the law mandates knowledge or a substitute (pointing) to validate the contract. In practice, if the parties fail to meet these conditions, the sale is fasid (voidable) due to gharar.
This principle applies across all sales unless a specific exception like salam (advance sale) is invoked.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا بد من معرفة قدر، ووصف ثمن غير مشار لا مشار.
كمصري أو دمشقي
- وهو المعتبر في الباب، إلا أنه لما كان باطناً أقيم الإيجاب والقبول مقامه؛ لدلالتهما على التراضي، والتعاطي دل على الرضا منهما، حتى لو صرح معه بعدم الرضا لم ينعقد ثم اختلفوا فيما يتم به التعاطي، قيل: يتم بالدفع من الجانبين، وأشار محمد إلى أنه يكتفي بتسليم المبيع. رمز الحقائق: ٣/٢] (فتح، كفاية) وأي قام أي أي واحد من المتعاقدين بطل الإيجاب: [لأن القيام دليل الإعراض والرجوع، فيبطل به كسائر عقود المبادلة، فلا يبقى للآخر ولاية القبول بعده] أي إذا قام أحد المتعاقدين عن المجلس بعد الإيجاب بطل الإيجاب؛ لأن القيام دليل الإعراض والرجوع، فيبطل العقد به كسائر عقود المبادلة بخلاف الخلع والعتق على مال، حيث لا يبطل بقيام الزوج والمولى؛ لأنه يمين من جهتهما والقبول شرط والأيمان لا تبطل بالقيام، وعند الشافعي: خيار القبول لا يمتد إلى آخر المجلس بل هو على الفور، قلنا: إن العاقد يحتاج إلى التردّي والتفكر، فيجعل ساعات المجلس كساعة واحدة وفيما قال الشافعي حرج بين، وهو مدفوع بالنص، قال تعالى: ﴿وَمَا جَعَلَ عَلَيْكُمْ فِي الدِّينِ مِنْ حَرَج ﴾ (الحج:٧٨) [رمز الحقائق: ٣/٢، ٤] (فتح) ولا بد إلخ: أي إذا كانت الأعواض غير مشار إليها سواء كانت ثمناً أو مبيعاً يشترط فيها معرفة مقدار الثمن، والمراد بالثمن الثمن المطلق وهو الدراهم والدنانير، وأما غيره فهو كالمبيع، ومعرفة هذين لابد منها؛ لأن جهالتهما تفضي إلى المنازعة (عيني، بر(جندي قدر أي قدر مبيع وثمن؛ لأن جهالتهما تفضي إلى المنازعة، فمعرفة قدر المبيع ككر حنطة وقفيز شعير، ومعرفة الثمن كخمسة دراهم وثلاثة دنانير. (عيني ، فتح) ووصف ثمن: اعلم أن إضافة الوصف إلى الثمن تشعر بأن معرفة الوصف شرط في الثمن فقط دون المبيع، بخلاف اشتراط معرفة القدر؛ فإنه بالنسبة لكل من المبيع ،والثمن ولهذا ذكر القدر مطلقا ولم يضفه لواحد منهما، ثم اعلم أن الدراهم والدنانير أثمان أبدا سواء قوبلت بغيرها أو بجنسها، وأما الأعيان القيمية فمبيعة أبداً، وأما الأعيان المثلية فإن قوبلت بالنقود فهي مبيعات أو بأمثالها فما كان موصوفاً بالذمة ثمن وما كان معيناً فمبيع، فإن كان كل منهما معيناً فما صحبه "الباء" أو "على" فهو ثمن، ومن حكم النقود أنها لا تتعين بالتعيين في عقود المعاوضات بل في المغصوب والأمانات والوكالات وكذا في كل عقد ليس معاوضة. غير مشار: بالجر صفة ثمن وقدر والحاصل أن الأعواض إذا كانت غير مشار إليها سواء كانت ثمناً أو مثمناً يشترط فيها معرفة المقدار في المبيع ومعرفة مقدار الثمن ووصفه؛ لأن جهالتهما تفضي إلى المنازعة كما في المسلم فيه فإن معرفة قدر المسلم فيه شرط لجواز عقد السلم. (عيني، فتح)
لا مشار: [ أي لا يشترط ذلك في مشار إليه لنفي الجهالة بالإشارة. (ط)] ضبطه الشمس الغزى بالرفع، ويقتضي الرفع كلام العيني أيضاً حيث قال: لا يحتاج إلى معرفة القدر في المبيع والثمن ووصفه الذي هو مشار إليه، .
'And it is necessary to know the quantity and description of the price, not the pointed (item).' 'Like Egyptian or Damascene.' '...The sum of the matter is that when the countervalues are not pointed to, whether they are price or priced, it is required to know the quantity of the sold item and the quantity and description of the price, because ignorance of them leads to dispute, as in salam where knowing the quantity of the salam commodity is a condition for the validity of the salam contract.' 'Non-pointed' is a description of 'price' and 'quantity'. 'Pointed' means that it is not required for a pointed item because pointing eliminates ignorance. Al-Ghazzi read it with nominative case, and al-Ayni's speech also implies that: that there is no need to know the quantity of the sold item and its description that is pointed to.
Source pages p. 251

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement clarifying the conditions for the countervalues (price and commodity) in a sale. The matn states that it is necessary (la budda) to know the quantity (qadr) and description (wasf) of the price (thaman) when the price is not physically pointed to (ghayr mushar). The commentary explains that if the items are not indicated by pointing, their quantity and description must be specified to avoid dispute. The price here refers to absolute price (al-thaman al-mutlaq), i.e., silver and gold coins (dirhams and dinars). Other items are considered as the commodity (muthman). The quantity must be known for both the commodity and the price, but the description (wasf) is only required for the price, not the commodity, as the word 'wasf' is specifically added to 'thaman'. The commentary further distinguishes between monetary species (naqd) and fungible goods (mithliyyat) vs. non-fungible (qimiyyat). Dirhams and dinars are always considered price, no matter what they are exchanged for. For fungibles, if exchanged against currency, they are the commodity; if exchanged against their type, the one described as a debt is price and the specific one is commodity. An important Hanafi rule: currency (nuqud) does not become specified by designation in commutative contracts (but does in cases of usurpation, trusts, agency, etc.). The exception: if the item is pointed to (mushar ilayh), then knowledge of quantity and description is not required because pointing eliminates ignorance.

Key Terms
ثمن (thaman): The price in a sale; in this context, specifically dirhams and dinars (silver and gold coins).
مبيع (mabī'): The sold commodity (muthman) in a sale.
مشار إليه (mushār ilayh): An item that is physically pointed at, thereby removing ignorance of its identity.
قدر (qadr): Quantity or measure of the item, e.g., weight, volume, count.
وصف (wasf): Description of the price, e.g., type, purity, minting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a sale of a bag of wheat, the price is 'one Egyptian dinar'. Both parties see the wheat and the coin. According to Hanafi fiqh, is the sale valid without specifying the exact weight of the dinar?
A) No, because the description of the price must be known.
B) Yes, because the coin is pointed to, so its description is not needed.
C) No, because the quantity of the wheat must be specified.
D) Yes, because the sale is by mutual delivery (ta'ati).

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, when the countervalues in a sale are not physically indicated, knowing the quantity of both and the description of the price is essential for validity; pointing obviates these requirements because it directly removes uncertainty.

Standing Up After Offer: Hanafi vs Shafi'i on Khiyar al-Qabul
Hanafi-Shafi'i dispute on khiyar al-qabul

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on khiyar al-qabul, explain the Shafi'i counterargument, and evaluate the Hanafi proof using Quran and analogy.

Core Idea
In a sale, the offer remains open until the session ends; standing up before acceptance voids it by indicating withdrawal.

This passage enters a classical dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools over the timing of acceptance in a contract of sale. The Hanafi school holds that the offer remains valid throughout the session (majlis al-'aqd), while the Shafi'i school insists that acceptance must be immediate. The Hanafi position is supported by analogy to other exchange contracts, an exception for khul' and manumission, and the Quranic principle that religion does not impose hardship.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling
Identify the core Hanafi rule: the offer becomes void if either party stands up before acceptance.
This is the mufta bihi position.
2
Identify the exception
Note that khul' and manumission for consideration are not voided by standing—they are treated as oaths.
This shows the ruling is not absolute.
3
State the Shafi'i position
Shafi'i holds that acceptance must be immediate; the option does not extend to the end of the session.
This is the opposing viewpoint.
4
Follow the Hanafi proof
Trace the dalil: the Quranic verse on no hardship and analogy to other exchange contracts.
The hardship principle supports the extended option.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: under Hanafi, acceptance can be delayed until the session ends; under Shafi'i, it must be immediate or the offer lapses.
This affects real transactions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب البيوع ما يتعلق بالبيع وأي قام عن المجلس قبل القبول بطل الإيجاب، [شرح:] وأي قام أي أي واحد من المتعاقدين بطل الإيجاب: [لأن القيام دليل الإعراض والرجوع، فيبطل به كسائر عقود المبادلة، فلا يبقى للآخر ولاية القبول بعده] أي إذا قام أحد المتعاقدين عن المجلس بعد الإيجاب بطل الإيجاب؛ لأن القيام دليل الإعراض والرجوع، فيبطل العقد به كسائر عقود المبادلة بخلاف الخلع والعتق على مال، حيث لا يبطل بقيام الزوج والمولى؛ لأنه يمين من جهتهما والقبول شرط والأيمان لا تبطل بالقيام، وعند الشافعي: خيار القبول لا يمتد إلى آخر المجلس بل هو على الفور، قلنا: إن العاقد يحتاج إلى التردّي والتفكر، فيجعل ساعات المجلس كساعة واحدة وفيما قال الشافعي حرج بين، وهو مدفوع بالنص، قال تعالى: ﴿وَمَا جَعَلَ عَلَيْكُمْ فِي الدِّينِ مِنْ حَرَج ﴾ (الحج:٧٨) [رمز الحقائق: ٣/٢، ٤] (فتح)
Book of Sales. Regarding that which relates to sale: And whoever stands up from the session before acceptance, the offer becomes void. [Commentary:] 'And whoever stands up' means any one of the two contracting parties, the offer becomes void: [because standing is evidence of turning away and retracting, so it becomes void by it like other contracts of exchange, so the other does not retain the authority of acceptance after it.] That is, if one of the two contracting parties stands up from the session after the offer, the offer becomes void; because standing is evidence of turning away and retracting, so the contract becomes void by it like other contracts of exchange, unlike khul' and manumission for a consideration, where it does not become void by the husband or the master standing up; because it is an oath from their side and acceptance is a condition, and oaths are not voided by standing. According to al-Shafi'i: the option of acceptance does not extend to the end of the session, rather it is immediate. We said: the contractor needs deliberation and thought, so the hours of the session are considered as one hour. What al-Shafi'i said involves hardship, and it is rebutted by the text, Allah says: 'And He has not placed upon you in religion any hardship' (al-Hajj:78).
Source pages p. 251

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the duration of the option of acceptance after an offer in a sales contract. The Hanafi position is that the offer remains valid until the end of the session (majlis al-'aqd), and if either party stands up before acceptance, the offer is void because standing indicates withdrawal. This is analogous to other exchange contracts. An exception is made for khul' and manumission for consideration, which are considered oaths and are not voided by standing. The Shafi'i school holds that the option of acceptance is immediate and does not extend to the end of the session. The Hanafi response is that the contractor needs time for deliberation, so the entire session is treated as one moment; to require immediate acceptance would cause hardship, which is prohibited by the Quranic verse. Thus, the Hanafi view is preferred.

Key Terms
إيجاب (ijab): The offer made by one contracting party in a sale.
قبول (qabul): The acceptance by the other party that completes the contract.
خيار القبول (khiyar al-qabul): The option for the offeree to accept or reject the offer during the session.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the legal effect if either party stands up from the session before acceptance?
A) The offer remains valid until the standing party returns.
B) The offer becomes void.
C) The offer becomes binding.
D) The offer is suspended until the next session.

Key Takeaway
In a sale, the offer is considered open until the session ends, and standing up before acceptance voids it—a rule that balances the need for deliberation with legal certainty.

Specifying Price When Not Pointed To
States conditions for specifying price when not pointed to; distinction between mushar and ghayr mushar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish when quantity and description of price must be specified in a sale, and apply the rule to distinguish pointed vs. non-pointed items.

Core Idea
Ignorance of price invalidates; when price is not pointed, specify quantity and description.

In a sale, if you can point to the item, its identity is clear. But when the item is absent or abstract, you must describe it precisely to avoid dispute. The Ḥanafī school lays down detailed rules for this, especially for the price (thaman). This passage from Kanz al-Daqāʾiq explains when description of price is mandatory and when it is not.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Determine whether the countervalues (price and merchandise) are mushar (pointed to) or ghayr mushar (not pointed to). The ruling hinges on this.
Pointing removes ignorance; no further description needed.
2
Check the requirement for the price
If the price is not pointed to, you must specify its quantity (e.g., 5 dirhams) and its description (e.g., full-weight dirhams).
Description is only required for the price, not for the merchandise.
3
Check the requirement for the merchandise
If the merchandise is not pointed to, you must only specify its quantity (e.g., a kurr of wheat). Description of quality is not required.
Quantity is required for both, description only for price.
4
Understand the rationale
Ignorance (jahāla) leads to dispute (munāzaʿa), which invalidates the contract due to gharar. This is why specification is necessary.
The rule is based on preventing conflict, similar to salam.
5
Apply the rule to dirhams/dinars and other assets
Dirhams and dinars are always thaman. If they are used as price, they must be described when not pointed to. Other goods follow the same logic but may switch roles depending on context.
Memory aid: 'Dirhams are always price; goods are always merchandise when exchanged for cash.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا بد من معرفة قدر، ووصف ثمن غير مشار لا مشار. ولا بد إلخ: أي إذا كانت الأعواض غير مشار إليها سواء كانت ثمناً أو مبيعاً يشترط فيها معرفة مقدار الثمن، والمراد بالثمن الثمن المطلق وهو الدراهم والدنانير، وأما غيره فهو كالمبيع، ومعرفة هذين لابد منها؛ لأن جهالتهما تفضي إلى المنازعة (عيني، بر(جندي قدر أي قدر مبيع وثمن؛ لأن جهالتهما تفضي إلى المنازعة، فمعرفة قدر المبيع ككر حنطة وقفيز شعير، ومعرفة الثمن كخمسة دراهم وثلاثة دنانير. (عيني ، فتح) ووصف ثمن: اعلم أن إضافة الوصف إلى الثمن تشعر بأن معرفة الوصف شرط في الثمن فقط دون المبيع، بخلاف اشتراط معرفة القدر؛ فإنه بالنسبة لكل من المبيع والثمن ولهذا ذكر القدر مطلقا ولم يضفه لواحد منهما، ثم اعلم أن الدراهم والدنانير أثمان أبدا سواء قوبلت بغيرها أو بجنسها، وأما الأعيان القيمية فمبيعة أبداً، وأما الأعيان المثلية فإن قوبلت بالنقود فهي مبيعات أو بأمثالها فما كان موصوفاً بالذمة ثمن وما كان معيناً فمبيع، فإن كان كل منهما معيناً فما صحبه "الباء" أو "على" فهو ثمن، ومن حكم النقود أنها لا تتعين بالتعيين في عقود المعاوضات بل في المغصوب والأمانات والوكالات وكذا في كل عقد ليس معاوضة. غير مشار: بالجر صفة ثمن وقدر والحاصل أن الأعواض إذا كانت غير مشار إليها سواء كانت ثمناً أو مثمناً يشترط فيها معرفة المقدار في المبيع ومعرفة مقدار الثمن ووصفه؛ لأن جهالتهما تفضي إلى المنازعة كما في المسلم فيه فإن معرفة قدر المسلم فيه شرط لجواز عقد السلم. (عيني، فتح) لا مشار: [ أي لا يشترط ذلك في مشار إليه لنفي الجهالة بالإشارة. (ط)] ضبطه الشمس الغزى بالرفع، ويقتضي الرفع كلام العيني أيضاً حيث قال: لا يحتاج إلى معرفة القدر في المبيع والثمن ووصفه الذي هو مشار إليه، .
It is necessary to know the quantity and the description of the price that is not pointed to; not that which is pointed to. [Commentary:] 'It is necessary, etc.' means: if the countervalues are not pointed to, whether they are price or merchandise, it is required to know the amount of the price. By 'price' is meant absolute price, which is dirhams and dinars. Anything other than these is like the merchandise. Knowledge of these two is necessary because ignorance of them leads to dispute. (Ayni, Burhan al-Din? Qadr means the quantity of merchandise and price; because ignorance of them leads to dispute. So knowledge of the quantity of merchandise, like a kurr of wheat or a qafiz of barley, and knowledge of the price, like five dirhams or three dinars. (Ayni, Fath) 'And description of the price': Know that adding description to the price indicates that knowledge of description is a condition for the price only, not for the merchandise, unlike the condition of knowing the quantity, for it pertains to both the merchandise and the price. For this reason, the quantity is mentioned absolutely and not attached to either. Then know that dirhams and dinars are always prices, whether exchanged for other things or for their own kind. As for valuable goods (qimiyyat), they are always merchandise. As for fungible goods (mithliyyat), if exchanged for cash, they are merchandise; if exchanged for their own kind, what is described in the dhimmah (debt) is the price, and what is specific is the merchandise. If both are specific, then what is accompanied by 'bi' or 'ala' is the price. Among the rulings of cash is that they are not determined by specification in contracts of exchange, but rather in cases of usurpation, trusts, and agencies, and similarly in any contract that is not an exchange. 'Non-pointed to' (ghayr mushar): in the genitive case describing 'price' and 'quantity'. The conclusion is that when the countervalues are not pointed to, whether price or priced, knowledge of the quantity in the merchandise and knowledge of the quantity and description of the price are required; because ignorance leads to dispute, as in salam, where knowledge of the quantity of the subject matter is a condition for the validity of the salam contract. (Ayni, Fath) 'Not pointed to' (la mushar): [i.e., this is not required for something pointed to, because pointing removes ignorance. (T)] Shams al-Ghazzi read it with nominative, and the reading of Ayni also implies nominative where he said: There is no need to know the quantity in the merchandise and the price and its description when it is pointed to.
Source pages p. 251

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof explaining the conditions for specifying the price and merchandise in a sales contract. The matn states that it is necessary to know the quantity and description of the price when the items are not pointed to (ghayr mushar ilayh), but not when they are pointed to (mushar ilayh). The commentary elaborates that 'price' here refers to dirhams and dinars as absolute price; other items are like merchandise. Knowledge of quantity is required for both merchandise and price, but description is only required for the price. This is because ignorance leads to dispute. The distinction between pointed and non-pointed items is that pointing removes ignorance, so no further specification is needed. Exceptions are made for ribawi items sold by weight or measure, and for the capital in salam if it is measured or weighed, where ignorance remains problematic despite pointing.

Key Terms
غير مشار (ghayr mushar): Something that is not pointed to; its quantity and description must be specified.
ثمن (thaman): Price in a sale; usually dirhams and dinars.
قدر (qadr): Quantity or amount, required for both merchandise and price when not pointed to.
وصف (wasf): Description, required only for the price when not pointed to.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a sale, when is it necessary to specify the description of the price?
A) When the price is pointed to
B) When the price is not pointed to
C) Always
D) Never

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi rule: for ghayr mushar items, quantity must be known for both price and merchandise, but description is required only for the price.

Cash or Credit Sales and Determining the Currency
Rules on cash/credit sales and when currency is unspecified; four scenarios when currencies differ.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for a valid cash or credit sale and apply the fourfold classification to determine the currency when unspecified.

Core Idea
A sale is valid with cash or a known term; unspecified currency defaults to the prevalent currency, but four scenarios govern when currencies differ.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq addresses two key issues in sales: the validity of cash and credit sales, and how to determine the currency when the price is stated absolutely (only quantity). The Hanafi school relies on custom (urf) to resolve ambiguity, and provides a detailed fourfold classification when multiple currencies exist in the land. Understanding these rules prevents disputes over payment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two valid forms of sale
The matn states that a sale is valid with a spot price (ḥāl) or with a known term (ajal ma‘lūm). Note that the term must be specified; an unknown term invalidates the sale.
The term is void upon the buyer's death, not the seller's.
2
Locate the proof for validity
The commentator cites the Quranic verse 'Allah has permitted sale' (al-Baqarah 2:275) as general permission, and the hadith of the Prophet buying from a Jew on credit and pawning his armor.
The proof establishes that credit sales are permissible, provided the term is known.
3
Understand the rule for absolute price
If the price is mentioned only by quantity (e.g., ten dirhams) without specifying the currency type, it defaults to the prevalent currency (al-naqd al-ghālib) of the land of the contract.
The land of the contract is considered, not the domicile of the parties.
4
Analyze the four scenarios when currencies differ
The passage outlines four cases based on equality/difference in value (māliyya) and circulation (rawāj). Identify each: (1) equal value and circulation → buyer chooses; (2) differ in both → default to prevalent; (3) differ in circulation only → default to more circulated; (4) differ in value only → sale invalid.
Invalidity in case 4 is due to unresolved ignorance (jahl) leading to dispute.
5
Determine the consequence of invalidity
If the sale is invalid (fāsid), it must be rescinded. The buyer cannot unilaterally decide the currency; the seller's consent is required even if some currencies are more circulated.
The commentary adds a note about mutual consent in the session.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وصح بثمن حال وبأجل معلوم، ومطلقه على النقد الغالب، وإن اختلف النقود، فسد إن لم يبين أحدها. [شرح:] بأجل معلوم [ أي مؤجل بأجل إذا كان بخلاف جنسه ولم يجمعهما قدر (ط)] أي يصح البيع إذا كان لأداء الثمن أجل معين، ومعناه: إذا بيع بخلاف جنسه ولم يجمعهما قدر؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَأَحَلَّ اللَّهُ الْبَيْعَ وَحَرَّمَ الرِّبا (البقرة: ٢٧٥) من غير فصل، وعنه عليها : أنه اشترى من يهودي إلى أجل ورهن درعه متفق عليه عن عائشة وليس فيه ذكر المبيع فأدرج صاحب الهداية طعاماً، وقيل: المبيع كان ثوبا، وقيد الأجل بالمعلوم؛ لأن البيع إلى الأجل المجهول فاسد ويبطل الأجل بموت المشتري لا البائع، ولو اختلفا في أصل الأجل فالقول لمنكره أو في قدره فلمدعي الأقل والبينة بينة المشتري في الوجهين. (فتح) ومطلقه إلخ [ أي الثمن أراد أن يكون مطلقاً : قيد البلد وعن قيد وصف الثمن بعد عشرة دراهم مثلا ( عيني)] أي ومن أطلق الثمن في البيع بأن ذكر القدر دون الصفة كان على غالب نقد البلد أي ينصرف البيع إلى التعامل به في بلده، سواء كان هو المتعامل به مع وجود دراهم أخرى لا يتعامل بها أو يتعامل بها إلا أن غيرها أكثر تعاملا. (فتح) الغالب أي في البلد؛ لأن المعلوم في العرف كالمعلوم بالنص والمراد بلد العقد لا بلد المتعاقدين. (ط) عيني) اختلف النقود في البلد وكانت في الرواج سواء وفي المالية مختلفة. (ط، عيني) فسد إن لم يبين إلخ: أي لو كانت النقود في البلد مختلفة، ولم يبين المشتري الثمن يفسد البيع؛ للجهالة المفضية إلى المنازعة، والمسألة رباعية الأولى: أن الدراهم استوت مالية ورواجاً، فالمشتري بالخيار دفع أي الدراهم شاء، الثانية: اختلفت مالية ورواجاً، فلينصرف إلى غالب نقد البلد الثالثة: اختلفت رواجاً فقط، فينصرف إلى الأروج، الرابعة: اختلفت مالية واستوت رواجاً، فسد البيع وهو منطوق المتن. (فتح) أحدها: في المجلس ويرضى به البائع وإن كان بعض النقود أروج ينصرف إليه. (ط)
And a sale is valid with a spot price and with a known term, and its absolute (unspecified) form refers to the prevalent currency of that land. And if currencies differ, the sale becomes invalid if one of them is not specified. [Commentary:] 'With a known term': [i.e., deferred by a term, when sold for something other than its kind and not combined by quantity (T)] Meaning: the sale is valid if there is a fixed term for payment of the price. Its meaning: when sold for something other than its kind and not combined by quantity; because of the verse: 'And Allah has permitted sale and forbidden usury' (al-Baqarah 275) without distinction. And from her (Aisha), it is reported that he (the Prophet) bought from a Jew on credit and pawned his armor, agreed upon (but the merchandise is not mentioned; the author of al-Hidayah added 'food', and it is said the merchandise was a garment). The term is qualified as 'known' because sale with an unknown term is invalid. The term becomes void with the death of the buyer, not the seller. If they differ regarding the existence of a term, the word is of the one who denies it; or regarding its length, the claimant of the lesser is favored, and the burden of proof is on the buyer in both cases. (Fath) 'And its absolute form, etc.': [i.e., he intended the price to be absolute: restricted to the land, rather than restricting the description of the price after ten dirhams, etc. (Ayni)] Meaning: whoever leaves the price absolute in a sale, mentioning only the quantity without description, it refers to the prevalent currency of that land. That is, the sale is interpreted according to what is customarily used in that land, whether it is the one circulated while other dirhams exist that are not used, or they are used but others are more common. (Fath) 'The prevalent (ghalib)': i.e., in the land, because what is known by custom is like what is known by text. The intended land is the place of the contract, not the place of the contracting parties. (T, Ayni) 'If the currencies differ in the land and are equal in circulation but differ in value.' (T, Ayni) 'It becomes invalid if not specified, etc.': i.e., if the currencies in the land are different and the buyer does not specify the price, the sale becomes invalid due to ignorance leading to dispute. The issue is fourfold: First: the dirhams are equal in value and circulation, then the buyer may pay any dirhams he wishes. Second: they differ in value and circulation, then it refers to the prevalent currency of the land. Third: they differ in circulation only, then it refers to the more circulated. Fourth: they differ in value but equal in circulation, then the sale is invalid, and this is the explicit meaning of the text. (Fath) 'One of them: in the session, and the seller is satisfied with it, even if some currencies are more circulated, it refers to that.' (T)
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage provides rulings on cash and credit sales and how to determine the currency when not specified. The matn states that a sale is valid with either cash or a known deferred term. When the price is mentioned absolutely (only quantity, no specification of currency), it defaults to the prevalent currency of the land of the contract. If multiple currencies exist in the land, the ruling depends on four scenarios: (1) if currencies are equal in value and circulation, the buyer may choose; (2) if they differ in both, it defaults to the prevalent one; (3) if only circulation differs, the more circulated is taken; (4) if values differ but circulation is equal, the sale is void due to unresolved ignorance. The proof includes the Quranic verse permitting sale and the practice of the Prophet. The commentary also notes that the term must be known, and disagreements about the term are settled by the one denying it or claiming the lesser, with the buyer bearing the burden of proof.

Key Terms
مطلق الثمن (mutlaq al-thaman): The price mentioned without specifying the currency type.
نقد البلد (naqd al-balad): The prevalent currency used in the land of the contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If in a sale, the price is stated as 'ten dirhams' without specifying the type of dirham, and in that city there are two types of dirhams equal in circulation but different in value, what is the ruling?
A) The sale is valid, and the buyer may pay either type
B) The sale is void
C) The sale is valid, and it refers to the prevalent type
D) The sale is suspended until the buyer specifies

Key Takeaway
When currencies differ, the validity depends on whether custom can resolve the ambiguity; custom works when circulation differs, but not when only values differ.

Selling Food by Measure or Estimation: Validity and Riba Considerations
Ruling on validity of estimation sale with riba conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state when selling food by estimation (juzaf) is valid or invalid according to the Hanafi school, and identify the exception for small amounts.

Core Idea
Estimation is valid for different genus; same genus needs equality or negligible quantity.

The matn states 'Yuba'u' (it is sold) without detail. The commentary clarifies that selling food by estimation is permissible when the genus differs, because pointing removes ignorance. However, when the genus is the same, estimation risks riba, so it is invalid unless equality is apparent or the amount is below half a sa'. Understanding these conditions is essential for lawful trade.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two methods of sale
Recognize that the matn mentions selling by measure (kaylan) and by estimation (juzafan). Estimation means without precise measurement or weight.
Juzaf may be vowelized with damm or kasr, both accepted.
2
Distinguish by genus
Apply the rule: estimation is valid if the food is exchanged for a different genus. Ignorance is removed by pointing. If the same genus, estimation is invalid due to potential riba.
This is based on the principle that equality of measure is required in ribawi exchanges.
3
Apply the exception for equality or small quantity
Even for same genus, estimation is valid if the two quantities are visibly equal in the session, or if the amount is less than half a sa'. Half a sa' is the minimum threshold for riba consideration.
The exception reflects the Hanafi position that riba only applies to amounts of half a sa' or more.
4
Note the internal disagreement
Imam Muhammad disliked even a date for two dates, holding that if much is forbidden, little is also forbidden. However, the relied-upon fatwa allows the small quantity exception.
This shows a legitimate ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school on the threshold.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويباع. [شرح:] ويباع إلخ: وفي البحر [٤٢٧/٥]: الفتوى على أن الطعام لا يخص الحنطة والدقيق، و"كيلا" تمييز أي من حيث الكيل، و"جزافاً" مثلث الجيم واقتصر في البحر والنهر على الضم، ونقل السيد الحموي عن مفتاح الأدب أنه بكسر الجيم هو المسموع، والجزاف في البيع والشراء ما يكون بلا كيل ولا وزن، ويصح إذا باعه بخلاف جنسه مجازفة؛ لأن صيرورة المبيع معلوماً بالمكايلة ظاهر، وأما في المجازفة فلأنه بالإشارة ترتفع الجهالة، وإن باع بجنسه مجازفة لا يجوز؛ لاحتمال الربا، إلا إذا ظهر تساويهما في المجلس، أو كان قليلا وهو ما دون نصف الصاع؛ لأن أدنى ما يكون مال الربا نصف صاع، وعن محمد أنه كره التمرة بالتمرتين، وقال: كل شيء حرم كثيره فالقليل منه حرام. [رمز الحقائق: ٥/٢] (فتح) بيع
And it is sold (yuba'u). [Commentary:] 'And it is sold, etc.' In al-Bahr [5/427]: The fatwa is that food is not restricted to wheat and flour. 'By measure' (kaylan) is a specification meaning in terms of measurement. 'By estimation' (juzafan) has three possible vowelizations; al-Bahr and al-Nahr restrict to dammah, and al-Sayyid al-Hamawi narrated from Miftah al-Adab that kasr is the heard. Juzaf in sale and purchase is that which is without measure or weight. It is valid if he sells it by estimation when it is of a different genus, because the sale of the merchandise becomes known by measurement, but in estimation, ignorance is removed by pointing. If he sells it by estimation when it is of the same genus, it is not permissible because of the possibility of usury, unless equality becomes apparent in the session, or it is a small amount, which is less than half a sa'; because the minimum amount for which usury is considered is half a sa'. From Muhammad that he disliked one date for two dates, and said: 'Everything whose much is forbidden, its little is also forbidden.' [Ramz al-Haqaiq: 5/2] (Fath) Baya' (sale).
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage deals with the ruling on selling food by measure (kaylan) or by estimation (juzafan). The matn states 'Yuba'u' (it is sold) without full detail, and the commentary explains. The fatwa is that 'food' here includes all types, not just wheat and flour. Selling by estimation is permissible when the food is exchanged for something of a different genus, because pointing removes ignorance; but when exchanged for the same genus, estimation is not allowed due to the risk of usury (riba). An exception is made if the quantities are visibly equal in the session, or if the amount is less than half a sa', as that is the minimum for riba. Imam Muhammad disliked even a date for two dates, adopting the principle that if much is forbidden, little is also forbidden. This reflects the Hanafi position on riba in sales.

Key Terms
جزاف (juzaf): Sale without precise measurement or weight; estimation by sight.
ربا (riba): Usury; prohibited excess in exchange of same genus items.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is selling food by estimation (juzafan) invalid according to the Hanafi school?
A) When exchanging for a different genus
B) When exchanging for the same genus unless equality is known or amount is below half a sa'
C) When the amount is less than half a sa'
D) Always

Key Takeaway
Sale by estimation of same genus food is invalid unless equality is known or the amount is below half a sa'.

Conditions of Valid Sale: Price and Deferred Payment
States conditions for sale with prompt/deferred payment and currency ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions for a valid sale concerning price and payment term, and apply the rule on currency default to determine validity.

Core Idea
A sale is valid with prompt or deferred payment at a known term; unspecified currency defaults to the prevalent one, but becomes void if multiple currencies exist and are not clarified.

This lesson focuses on the foundational conditions of the price (thaman) in a sale contract according to the Hanafi school. The matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq presents three concise rules: the price can be paid immediately or at a known future date; if the currency is not specified, the prevalent local currency is assumed; but if multiple currencies circulate and the parties do not specify, the sale is void due to uncertainty. Understanding these rules helps you evaluate the validity of many everyday transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three rulings in the passage
Read the Arabic matn and its translation. Spot each distinct rule: (1) sale valid with prompt price, (2) sale valid with known term, (3) unspecified price defaults to prevalent currency, but if currencies differ and not specified, sale is void.
These rules are independent conditions for validity.
2
Classify each rule as condition or consequence
For rules (1) and (2), note that they state conditions under which a sale is valid. For rule (3), note that it first gives a default (condition met) and then a consequence of failure to specify when multiple currencies exist.
Understanding the structure helps apply rules correctly.
3
Link each rule to its legal basis
The permission for deferred payment is based on Quran 2:275 and the Prophet's practice. The currency default is based on custom (urf), which has legal weight. The invalidity when currencies differ is based on eliminating gharar.
Dalil is important for deeper comprehension.
4
Apply the rules to a concrete scenario
Take an example: A buyer in a country with two equally used currencies agrees to pay '100' without specifying. According to rule (3), since currencies differ and no specification, the sale is void. If only one currency exists, it's valid and payment is in that currency.
Application solidifies understanding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وصح بثمن حال وبأجل معلوم، ومطلقه على النقد الغالب، وإن اختلف النقود، فسد إن لم يبين
And a sale is valid with a prompt price and with a known term, and its absolute [mention of price] is [construed] according to the prevalent currency, and if currencies differ, it becomes void if [the price] is not specified.
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It lays down three rules for the validity of a sale concerning the price (thaman) and deferred payment (ajal). First, a sale is valid if the price is paid immediately (hal) or if payment is deferred to a known future date (ajal ma'lum). Second, if the buyer mentions only the amount of the price without specifying the type of currency, the sale defaults to the prevalent currency of the country where the contract takes place. Third, if there are multiple currencies in circulation and the price is not clarified, the sale is void due to excessive uncertainty leading to dispute. The commentary from Fath al-Qadir explains that the evidence for the permissibility of deferred payment is the Quranic verse "And Allah has permitted trade and prohibited usury" (2:275) and the hadith that the Prophet bought food from a Jew on credit with a known term, pawning his armor. The condition that the term be known is essential because sale with an unknown term is void. The ruling on currency is based on custom ('urf), which is considered like textual stipulation.

Key Terms
ثمن حال (thaman hal): A price paid immediately at the time of the contract.
أجل معلوم (ajal ma'lum): A known future date for payment.
النقد الغالب (al-naqd al-ghalib): The prevalent currency in the country of the contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens if a buyer agrees to pay '100 dirhams' but the country has multiple currencies equally in circulation and the parties do not specify which currency?
A) The sale is valid, and the buyer may pay in any currency.
B) The sale is void because of uncertainty.
C) The sale is valid, and the buyer must pay in the most prevalent currency.
D) The sale is suspended until the currency is agreed.

Key Takeaway
A sale is valid only if the price is either paid immediately or deferred to a known term, and if the currency is not specified, it defaults to the prevalent currency; but if multiple currencies exist and are not clarified, the sale is void.

Selling Food by Measure, Guess, or Unknown Container
Ruling on selling food by measure or by guess and by a specific container or stone of unknown capacity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on selling food by guess or by an unknown container, and identify the conditions and exceptions that affect validity.

Core Idea
Selling food by guess is permissible when uncertainty does not lead to dispute; custom may override strict measurement requirements except in riba transactions.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq addresses a practical market reality: buying and selling food without precise measurement. The Hanafi school, known for considering custom ('urf), permits such transactions under certain conditions. We will explore when guessing quantity is valid and when it is prohibited, and understand the role of istihsan in facilitating commerce.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is selling food. The ruling is that it is permissible (ja'iz) whether sold by exact measure, by guess, or by a specific container of unknown capacity.
The default permissibility is broad, but exceptions exist.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The proof is istihsan (juristic preference) based on prevalent custom. Custom removes the uncertainty that would otherwise make the transaction void due to gharar.
No explicit primary text is cited; it is a reliance on 'urf.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (how the proof supports the ruling)
Custom (selling by guess and by containers) is a widespread practice that does not lead to disputes. Therefore, the prohibition based on uncertainty is lifted by istihsan.
The principle is 'al-gharar al-yasir yu'fu 'anhu' (minor uncertainty is overlooked).
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Hasan ibn Ziyad narrated from Abu Hanifa that selling by an unknown container is not valid. However, the majority of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and later authorities uphold permissibility.
This is a case of nawadir vs. zahir al-riwayah.
5
Evaluate the tarjih and mufta bihi
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is permissibility, due to custom and the majority view. The author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq and its commentators adopt this.
The tarjih is based on the strength of custom and the weakness of the contrary narration.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويباع الطعام كيلاً وجزافاً، وبإناء أو حجر بعينه لم يدر قدره
And food is sold by measure and by guess, and by a specific container or stone whose capacity is not known.
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement that expands on the modes of selling food. The text states that food can be sold either by exact measure (kaylan) or by guess (juzafan), and also by using a specific container or stone as a measure, even if its exact capacity is unknown. The commentary explains that 'food' in Hanafi legal custom includes wheat, its flour, and all grains like lentils and chickpeas. Selling by guess (juzaf) is permissible when the food is sold against a different genus (e.g., food for money) because the object becomes known through pointing, and any remaining ignorance of exact quantity does not lead to dispute. However, if food is sold against its own genus (e.g., wheat for wheat), guesswork is not allowed due to the risk of riba, unless the two quantities are known to be equal in the session, or the amount is less than half a sa' (since small amounts are not considered ribawi). Selling by a specific container (like a bowl) or stone is valid provided the container does not compress or expand significantly; otherwise, it is not allowed except for water skins by istihsan due to custom. The commentary notes that Abu Hanifa's student Hasan ibn Ziyad narrated that selling by a stone weight or an unknown container is not valid because it is guesswork, but the relied-upon position is permissibility due to custom.

Key Terms
جزافاً (juzafan): Selling by guess without measuring or weighing.
الطعام (al-ta'am): In Hanafi custom, primarily wheat and its flour, but includes all grains like lentils, chickpeas, etc.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is selling food by guess (juzaf) permissible according to the Hanafi school?
A) Only when the food is wheat or its flour.
B) When the food is sold against a different genus (e.g., for money).
C) Only if the exact quantity is known through measurement.
D) When the food is sold against its own genus.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, selling food by guess or by an unknown container is permissible based on custom, as long as it does not involve riba or significant uncertainty leading to dispute.

Sale of Food by Estimation and by a Specific Container or Stone
Explaining the ruling on selling food by estimation and by a specific container or stone with conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for the validity of selling food by estimation (jizaf) and by a specific container or stone, and apply the Hanafi rule distinguishing compressible and non-compressible containers.

Core Idea
Selling by estimation is valid; non-compressible containers are valid, compressible ones invalid except water skins by istihsan.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq explains the Hanafi ruling on selling food without exact measure, either by estimation or using a specific container or stone of unknown capacity. The ruling hinges on whether the method leads to dispute. You will learn the key conditions and the exception based on customary practice (istihsan).

Guided Path
1
Identify the types of sale discussed
The passage covers sale by measure, by estimation (jizaf), and by a specific container or stone.
Jizaf is selling by guess without exact measure or weight.
2
Understand the definition of food in this context
Food is defined in custom as wheat, flour, and grains like lentils and chickpeas.
This definition is specific to the chapter of sales.
3
Analyze the condition for jizaf
Jizaf is valid because the item becomes known through estimation; the condition is that the item is identifiable and pointed to.
The hadith 'The Prophet (ﷺ) forbade selling food until it is measured' is not directly cited, but the permissibility is based on custom.
4
Examine the rule for container/stone sale
If the container is non-compressible (like a bowl), the sale is valid; if compressible (like a basket), invalid except for water skins by istihsan. Similarly for crumbling stones.
The distinction is based on whether ignorance leads to dispute.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Hasan ibn Ziyad reported a stricter view from Abu Hanifa disallowing such sales, but the relied-upon position is the majority's permissibility.
The mufta bihi follows the general permissibility with conditions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الطعام كيلاً وجزافاً، وبإناء أو حجر بعينه لم يدر قدره.
الطعام: وهو في العرف الحنطة ودقيقها، وكل حبوب كالعدس والحمص وأمثالهما. (معدن)
وجزافاً: أي يباع أيضاً جزافاً، بكسر الجيم معرب گزاف هو أخذ الشيء بالخرص بلا كيل ولا وزن؛ لأن بكل منهما يصير المبيع معلوماً. (عيني، معدن)
وبإناء: أي ويباع الطعام بإناء بعينه الأن هذه الجهالة لا تفضي إلى المنازعة] وهذا إذا كان الإناء لا ينكبس بالتكبيس، ولا ينقبض ولا ينبسط كالقصعة والخزف، وأما إذا كان ينكبس كالزنبيل والقفة فلا يجوز إلا في قرب الماء استحساناً؛ للتعامل فيه، وكذا إذا كان الحجر يتفتت، وكذا إذا باعه بوزن شيء يخفّ إذا جفّ كالخيار والبطيخ، وروى الحسن عن أبي حنيفة أن البيع لا يجوز بوزن حجر، ولا بإناء لا يعرف مقداره. رمز الحقائق: ٥/٢] لأن هذا جزاف، وشرط جوازه أن يكون مميزاً مشاراً إليه، وإنما خص الحجر والإناء بالذكر؛ لأن المسألة فيما لا يحتمل الزيادة والنقصان. (مسكين)
The book of sales: Food by measure and by estimation, and by a specific container or stone whose capacity is unknown. Food: In custom it means wheat and its flour, and all grains like lentils, chickpeas, and the like. (Ma'din) And by estimation: That is, it may be sold also by estimation, pronounced with kasr of jim, a Persian word meaning taking something by guess without measure or weight, because by each of these the sold item becomes known. (Ayni, Ma'din) And by a container: Meaning food may be sold by a specific container, now this ignorance does not lead to dispute, and this is when the container does not compress when packed, does not contract nor expand, like a bowl and earthenware. But if it compresses like a basket or bag, it is not permissible except for water skins by istihsan, due to custom. Similarly if the stone crumbles, and similarly if sold by weight of something that lightens when dried like cucumber and watermelon. Al-Hasan reported from Abu Hanifa that the sale is not allowed by weight of a stone, nor by a container whose capacity is unknown. Ramz al-Haqa'iq 5/2, because this is jizaf, and its condition of permissibility is that it is distinct and pointed to. The mention of stone and container is specific because the matter concerns what does not bear increase or decrease. (Miskin)
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on selling food by estimation (jizaf) and by a specific container or stone. The author first defines 'food' in the Hanafi custom as wheat, flour, and similar grains. Then he explains jizaf: selling by guess without exact measure or weight, which is permissible because the item becomes known. The main focus is on selling by a container or stone of unknown capacity. The ruling distinguishes based on the nature of the container: if it is rigid (like a bowl or earthenware) and does not compress, the sale is valid because the ignorance does not lead to dispute. If it is compressible (like a basket or bag), it is invalid except for water skins due to custom (istihsan). Similarly, if the stone crumbles, it is invalid. The narrator al-Hasan ibn Ziyad reports that Abu Hanifa did not permit such sales at all, but the relied-upon position is the first. The condition for jizaf is that the item must be identifiable and pointed to. The commentary concludes that the mention of stone and container is only for items that do not accept increase or decrease (i.e., they are fixed volumes).

Key Terms
جزافاً (jizāfan): Selling by estimation without exact measure or weight.
إناء (inā’): A container used for measuring food in sale.
استحسان (istihsān): Juridical preference overriding qiyas due to custom or necessity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is selling food by a specific container invalid according to the text?
A) When the container is compressible like a basket
B) When the container is a water skin
C) When the container is made of stone
D) When the container is large

Key Takeaway
Selling food by estimation or by a non-compressible container is valid in Hanafi fiqh, provided the item is identifiable; compressible containers are invalid except for water skins by istihsan.

The Sale of 'Each' (Kull) in Hanafi Jurisprudence: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on 'kull' contract validity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on selling by 'each' (kull) and explain why the fatwa favors the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
When total is unknown, 'each' sells only one unit for fungibles (Abu Hanifa) but all units by fatwa for ease.

This lesson examines a key intra-Hanafi dispute: selling a heap of grain 'each sa' by a dirham' or a flock 'each sheep by a dirham'. The matn states the sale is valid only for one sa' or invalid entirely. However, the Sahibayn disagree, and the fatwa follows them to facilitate transactions. Let's analyze the reasoning and practical consequence.

Guided Path
1
State the three scenarios
Identify the three types: subrah (heap of grain), thalla (flock), and cloth (thawb). Each sold with 'kull' (each unit) and price per unit.
These represent fungible (like grain), non-fungible identical (like sheep varying), and divisible goods (cloth).
2
Identify Abu Hanifa's ruling and principle
For subrah: valid only for one sa'. For thalla and cloth: invalid entirely. His principle: 'kull' with unknown total indicates one unit; but for non-fungibles, even one is invalid due to variation or harm.
He analogizes to selling cloth by its number (raqm), which is impermissible by consensus.
3
Identify Sahibayn's ruling and proof
They rule valid for all units in all scenarios. Their dalil: the object is known by pointing; ignorance of quantity can be removed by measuring in the session, like jizaf (sale by estimation).
They emphasize ease of removing ignorance.
4
Analyze the Hanafi rebuttal
Abu Hanifa responds: the ability to remove ignorance after contract does not validate the contract before removal. The cloth-by-raqm consensus proves this.
The dispute hinges on whether post-contract measurement cures initial ignorance.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and rationale
The fatwa is with the Sahibayn for ease (taysiran 'ala al-nas), as stated in al-Hidayah. So today, selling 'each sa' by dirham' is valid for all sa's.
This is a classic example of tarjih based on public benefit.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن باع صبرة كل صاع بدرهم صح في صاع، ولو باع ثلة أو ثوبا كل شاة أو ذراع بدرهم فسد في الكل، وبه يفتي.
صبرة: الصبرة بالضم هي جملة من الطعام بلا كيل ووزن. (ط،فتح) كل صاع بالنصب بدل من "صبرة"، أي باع كل صاع من صبرة. (عيني) صح في صاع: [واحد إلا أن يسمي جملة صيعانها أي صح البيع في صاع واحد عند أبي حنيفة؛ لأنه معلوم والباقي مجهول مع الخيار للمشتري؛ لتفرق الصفقة عليه دون البائع وقالا يجوز في الكل؛ لأن المبيع معلوم بالإشارة والمشار إليه لا يحتاج إلى معرفة قدره، وجهالة الثمن بيدهما رفعها بأن يكيلاه في المجلس، وما هو كذلك لا يفضي إلى المنازعة، وله: أن الثمن مجهول، وذلك مفسد، ولا جهالة في القفيز الواحد، فصح فيه وكون العاقدين بيدهما إزالة الجهالة لا البيع قبل إزالتها، بدلالة الإجماع على عدم جواز بيع الثوب برقمه وهو بسكون القاف علامة يعرف بها مقدار ما وقع به البيع من الثمن مع أن بيد البائع إزالتها، وظاهر "الهداية" ترجيح قولهما، وبه يفتي تيسيراً على الناس، فإن سمى البائع جملة الصيعان أوكيل الصبرة في المجلس صح البيع وثبت الخيار للمشتري. (عيني، فتح)
ولو باع ثلة بفتح الثاء المثلثة وتشديد اللام: هي القطع من الغنم] وهي في اللغة قطيع الغنم، والحكم يعم الإبل والبقر، وكل ما في تبعيضه ضرر كالمصنوع من الأواني وكذا كل عددي متفاوت.
فسد في الكل: أي عند أبي حنيفة؛ لأن الأصل عنده أن كلمة "كل" متى أضيفت إلى ما لم يعلم منتهاه تتناول الواحد، فعلى هذا كان أن أدناه من وهو في شاة واحدة كما في صاع واحد لكن لما كان كل واحد ينبغي يصح الشياه متفاوتة لم يجز في الواحد أيضاً، بخلاف صاع واحد من الصبرة لعدم التفاوت فيها، وقطع ذراع من الثوب ضرر على البائع فلا يجوز أيضاً، كما لو باع جذعاً من سقف، وعندهما: يجوز في الكل، والدليل ما مر.(فتح، چلپی) ثوبا أو باع ثوبا مشاراً إليه يضره القطع. (ط)
ولو سمى الكل صح في الكُل، فلو نقص كيل أخذ بحصته أو فسخ، وإن زاد كيل فيما ذكرنا فللبائع، ولو نقص ذراع أخذ بكل الثمن أو ترك، وإن زاد فللمشتري.
ولو سمى الكل: أي كل المبيع والثمن في المجلس في هذه المسائل الثلاث - الصبرة والثلة والثوب – صح البيع سواء كان التسمية عند العقد أو بعده والحاصل أن شرط الجواز أحد الأمرين: إما العلم بجملة الثمن وإن لم يعلم عدد المعقود عليه، أو العلم بعدد المعقود عليه وإن لم يعلم جملة الثمن؛ لأن العلم بثمن كل واحد من الشياه أو الذرعان يغني عن التصريح بجملة الثمن، فلو قال: بعت منك هذه العشرة أغنام أو هذا الثوب وهو عشرة أذرع، أو قال بعت منك هذه الأغنام أو هذا الثوب بعشرة، كل شاة أو ذراع بدرهم، جاز اتفاقاً . (فتح) في الكل: أي في المسائل الثلاث؛ لزوال المانع. (ط) عيني)
نقص كيل: فيما لو اشترى صبرة على أنها مائة صاع بمائة درهم. (ط) أخذ بحصته إلخ : أي لو نقص كيل فيما إذا باع صبرة وسمى جملتها، ثم وجدها ناقصة، أخذ الباقي بحصته من الثمن؛ لأن الثمن ينقسم بالأجزاء على أجزاء المبيع المثلي مكيلاً أو موزوناً لا القيمي، أو فسخ البيع لفوات الصفة، وكذا كل مكيل أو موزون ليس في تبعيضه ضرر. (عيني، فتح) فللبائع أي فالزائد للبائع؛ لأنه لم يدخل في البيع إلا القدر المسمى، فبقي الزيادة على ملكه، والقدر ليس بوصف حتى يتبع الأصل. (عيني)
ذراع: فيما إذا باع مذروعا وسمى جملة الذرعان ولم يسم لكل ذراع ثمناً. (عيني) لأن الذراع وصف؛ لأنه عبارة عن الطول والعرض، والوصف لا يقابله شيء من الثمن كأطراف الحيوان. ثم اعلم أن المشايخ ذكروا في الفرق بين الأصل والوصف حدوداً، فقيل: إن ما يتعيب بالتبعيض والتشقيص، فالزيادة والنقصان فيه وصف، وما لا يتعيب فالزيادة والنقصان فيه أصل، وقيل: الوصف ما لوجوده تأثير في تقويم غيره، ولعدمه تأثير في نقصان غيره، والأصل ما لا يكون بهذه المثابة. وقيل: إن ما لا ينتقص قيمة الباقي بفواته فهو أصل وما ينتقص قيمة الباقي بفواته فهو وصف، فعلم في المكيلات والموزونات أصل والذراع في المذروعات وصف، فإذا انتقص قفيز من مائة قفيز لا يتعيب الباقي، ويشتري الباقي بحصته من الثمن، واليد والعين إذا فاتتا ينتقص قيمة النفس، فلا يشترى الباقي بالثمن الذي كان يشتري معه بحصته ما نقص، وكذا الذراع الواحد من الثوب أو الدار إذا فات، فيأخذ إن شاء بكل الثمن أو ترك. (كفاية، فتح) أو ترك والأصل فيه أن الذراع في المذروعات وصف والكيل في المكيلات أصل، فلا ينقسم الثمن على الأوصاف إلا عند التعيين، إلا أنه يثبت له الخيار لفوات الوصف المرغوب فيه. (عيني) فللمشتري: أي فهو للمشتري بذلك الثمن؛ لأن الذراع وصف لا يقابله شيء من الثمن. (ط، عيني)
And whoever sells a heap, each sa' by a dirham, it is valid for one sa'. And if he sells a flock or a cloth, each sheep or each cubit by a dirham, it is invalid in all, and by this fatwa is given. A heap (subrah): a heap with damm is a pile of food without measure or weight. 'Each sa'' is in accusative as a substitute for 'heap', meaning he sold each sa' from a heap. 'Valid for one sa'': one, unless he specifies the total number of its sa's, i.e., the sale is valid for one sa' according to Abu Hanifa because it is known while the rest is unknown, with the buyer having the option, because the contract is split upon him not the seller. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say it is valid in all, because the sold item is known by pointing and the pointed-to does not need knowledge of its quantity, and the ignorance of the price is in their hands to remove by measuring it in the session, and what is like that does not lead to dispute. His (Abu Hanifa's) proof: the price is unknown and that is corrupting, and there is no ignorance in the single qafiz, so it is valid in it. The fact that the contracting parties have the ability to remove ignorance does not validate the sale before removal, as evidenced by the consensus on the non-permissibility of selling a cloth by its number (raqm), which is a mark by which the amount of the price is known, even though the seller can remove it. The apparent meaning of al-Hidayah favors their view, and by it fatwa is given for ease for the people. If the seller specifies the total of the sa's or measures the heap in the session, the sale is valid and the buyer's option is established. (Ayni, Fath) And if he sells a flock (thalla) with fatha of tha and tashdid of lam: it is a portion of sheep; in language a flock of sheep, and the ruling includes camels and cattle, and everything in which division causes harm, like manufactured vessels, and similarly every countable item that varies. 'Invalid in all' means according to Abu Hanifa, because his principle is that the word 'each' when added to something whose limit is not known takes one. On this basis, it would be valid for one sheep as for one sa', but because each sheep differs in value, it is not permissible for one either, unlike one sa' from a heap due to the lack of variation there. And cutting a cubit from a cloth harms the seller, so it is not permissible either, like selling a beam from a ceiling. According to the two (Sahibayn), it is valid in all, and the proof is what has preceded. (Fath, Chalpi) Or he sells a cloth pointed to that cutting harms it. (T) And if he specifies the total, it is valid in all. Then if there is a shortage in measure, he takes his portion or cancels; if there is an excess in measure in what we mentioned, it is for the seller. And if there is a shortage in cubit, he takes the entire price or leaves; if there is an excess, it is for the buyer. 'And if he specifies the total': meaning the total of the sold and the price in the session in these three cases – the heap, the flock, and the cloth – the sale is valid whether the specification is at the contract or after. The gist is that the condition of permissibility is one of two things: either knowledge of the total price even if the quantity of the object is unknown, or knowledge of the quantity of the object even if the total price is unknown; because knowledge of the price of each sheep or cubit suffices for stating the total price. For example, if he says 'I sold you these ten sheep' or 'this cloth which is ten cubits', or 'I sold you these sheep or this cloth for ten, each sheep or cubit for a dirham', it is valid by agreement. (Fath) 'In all' means in the three cases, due to the removal of the impediment. (T, Ayni) 'Shortage in measure' concerns when he bought a heap as one hundred sa' for one hundred dirhams. (T) 'He takes his portion etc.': meaning if there is a shortage in measure when he sold a heap and specified its total, then found it short, he takes the remaining by its portion of the price, because the price divides into parts over the parts of the sold item if it is mithli (fungible) by measure or weight, not qimi (non-fungible); or he cancels the sale due to loss of the desired attribute. Similarly for every weighed or measured item in whose division there is no harm. (Ayni, Fath) 'For the seller' means the excess is for the seller, because only the specified amount entered the sale, so the excess remains his property, and the amount is not a description to follow the origin. (Ayni) 'Cubit' concerns when he sells a measured-by-length item and specified the total cubits but did not specify a price for each cubit. (Ayni) Because the cubit is a description, as it expresses length and width, and the description is not compensated by any part of the price, like limbs of an animal. Then know that the scholars mentioned definitions for the difference between origin and description. Some said: what is damaged by division and partition, increase and decrease in it is a description, and what is not damaged, increase and decrease in it is an origin. Others said: the description is that whose existence affects the valuation of others and whose absence affects the deficiency of others, and the origin is not like that. Others said: what does not diminish the value of the remainder by its loss is an origin, and what diminishes the value of the remainder by its loss is a description. Thus it is known that in measured and weighed items, the standard is an origin, and the cubit in length-measured items is a description. So if a qafiz is missing from a hundred qafiz, the remainder is not defective, and the remainder is bought with its portion of the price. But if a hand or eye is lost, the value of the self diminishes, so the remainder is not bought with the portion that would have been the price for what was lost. Similarly, if one cubit of a cloth or house is lost, he takes the entire price or leaves. (Kifaya, Fath) And the origin is that the cubit in length-measured items is a description and the measure in measured items is an origin, so the price does not divide over descriptions unless specified, but he has the option due to the loss of the desired attribute. (Ayni) 'For the buyer' means it is for the buyer with that price, because the cubit is a description that is not compensated by any part of the price. (T, Ayni)
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage covers rules for selling items per unit (each sa', each sheep, each cubit) and the consequences of shortfall or excess. The matn states: selling a heap (subrah) 'each sa' by a dirham' is valid only for one sa' according to Abu Hanifa; selling a flock (thallah) each sheep or a cloth each cubit is invalid in all. The fatwa is given by the latter. The commentary details the intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa argues that the price of the remaining units is unknown, corrupting the contract, and analogy to selling cloth by its number supports his view. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say the sale is valid in all because the object is known by pointing, and ignorance can be removed by measuring in the session; they also analogize to the permissibility of jizaf. The fatwa follows the Sahibayn for ease. For the flock and cloth, Abu Hanifa rules total invalidity because of variation in value and harm from cutting; the Sahibayn allow all with the same reasoning. If the total is specified (e.g., ten sheep for ten dirhams), the sale is valid by agreement. Then the commentary turns to shortfall and excess: for measured (makil/mawzun) goods, if the actual amount falls short, the buyer takes the remainder with a proportional price or cancels; if excess, the seller keeps it. For length-measured (madhru') goods like cloth, if short, the buyer takes the entire cloth at full price or cancels; if excess, the buyer gets it free because the cubit is a description, not an origin. The scholars define 'asl' (origin) as what does not diminish the value of the remainder when missing, and 'wasf' (description) as what does diminish it. Applied: measure in grain is asl, cubit in cloth is wasf.

Key Terms
صبرة (ṣubrah): A heap of food without specified measure or weight.
ثلة (thallah): A flock of sheep or a portion of a herd.
كل (kull): Each; when added to an unknown total, it indicates one per the Hanafi principle unless specified otherwise.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the fatwa (mufta bihi), when someone sells a heap of grain saying 'each sa' by a dirham', how many sa's are sold?
A) Only one sa'
B) All sa's
C) None, the sale is void
D) It depends on the buyer's choice

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi fatwa permits selling by 'each' when price per unit is stated, validating the entire transaction for ease, despite Abu Hanifa's stricter view.
