Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
8 min
Shortfall and Excess in Sales: The Asl-Wasf Distinction in Hanafi Fiqh
Rulings on shortfall/excess with asl-wasf distinction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rules for shortfall and excess in measured and length-measured goods, distinguishing between asl (origin) and wasf (description).

Core Idea
In sales with specified total, shortage in measured goods is compensated proportionally; shortage in length-measured goods voids the sale unless full price is paid.

This lesson covers the Hanafi rulings when a contract specifies the total quantity of the item, but the actual delivered quantity differs. The key is the distinction between asl (origin) and wasf (description). For measured (makil/mawzun) goods, the unit is an origin, so a shortfall allows proportional reduction or cancellation. For length-measured (madhru') goods, the unit is a description, so a shortfall gives the buyer only two options: pay full price or cancel. Excess also differs accordingly.

Guided Path
1
Understand the definitions of asl and wasf
Asl (origin): something whose loss does not diminish the value of the remainder (e.g., a qafiz of grain from a hundred). Wasf (description): something whose loss diminishes the value of the remainder (e.g., a cubit of cloth from a piece).
The passage gives three definitions; the operative one is based on value impact.
2
Apply asl/wasf to measured goods (makil/mawzun)
If the actual delivered quantity is less than specified, the buyer takes the remainder with a proportional reduction in price, or cancels. If excess, the seller keeps it.
Example: bought 100 sa' for 100 dirhams, found 90. Buyer pays 90 dirhams for 90 sa' or cancels.
3
Apply asl/wasf to length-measured goods (madhru')
If the actual delivered length is less than specified, the buyer either pays the full price (takes all) or cancels. No proportional reduction. If excess, the buyer gets it free.
Example: bought 10 cubits of cloth for 10 dirhams, found 9. Buyer pays 10 dirhams and takes 9 cubits, or cancels.
4
Identify the rationale: harm from division
For measured goods, dividing does not harm the remainder; for length-measured goods, cutting a piece damages the whole cloth, so the buyer cannot take just a part at a proportional price.
The hand and eye analogy illustrates: loss of a limb reduces whole body value.
5
Apply to non-fungible goods (qimi)
For goods that are not fungible (e.g., animals), the price does not divide proportionally; shortfall gives full price or cancel, similar to length-measured.
The text mentions 'qimi' goods are different from mithli.

ومن باع صبرة كل صاع بدرهم صح في صاع، ولو باع ثلة أو ثوبا كل شاة أو ذراع بدرهم فسد في الكل، وبه يفتي.
صبرة: الصبرة بالضم هي جملة من الطعام بلا كيل ووزن. (ط،فتح) كل صاع بالنصب بدل من "صبرة"، أي باع كل صاع من صبرة. (عيني) صح في صاع: [واحد إلا أن يسمي جملة صيعانها أي صح البيع في صاع واحد عند أبي حنيفة؛ لأنه معلوم والباقي مجهول مع الخيار للمشتري؛ لتفرق الصفقة عليه دون البائع وقالا يجوز في الكل؛ لأن المبيع معلوم بالإشارة والمشار إليه لا يحتاج إلى معرفة قدره، وجهالة الثمن بيدهما رفعها بأن يكيلاه في المجلس، وما هو كذلك لا يفضي إلى المنازعة، وله: أن الثمن مجهول، وذلك مفسد، ولا جهالة في القفيز الواحد، فصح فيه وكون العاقدين بيدهما إزالة الجهالة لا البيع قبل إزالتها، بدلالة الإجماع على عدم جواز بيع الثوب برقمه وهو بسكون القاف علامة يعرف بها مقدار ما وقع به البيع من الثمن مع أن بيد البائع إزالتها، وظاهر "الهداية" ترجيح قولهما، وبه يفتي تيسيراً على الناس، فإن سمى البائع جملة الصيعان أوكيل الصبرة في المجلس صح البيع وثبت الخيار للمشتري. (عيني، فتح)
ولو باع ثلة بفتح الثاء المثلثة وتشديد اللام: هي القطع من الغنم] وهي في اللغة قطيع الغنم، والحكم يعم الإبل والبقر، وكل ما في تبعيضه ضرر كالمصنوع من الأواني وكذا كل عددي متفاوت.
فسد في الكل: أي عند أبي حنيفة؛ لأن الأصل عنده أن كلمة "كل" متى أضيفت إلى ما لم يعلم منتهاه تتناول الواحد، فعلى هذا كان أن أدناه من وهو في شاة واحدة كما في صاع واحد لكن لما كان كل واحد ينبغي يصح الشياه متفاوتة لم يجز في الواحد أيضاً، بخلاف صاع واحد من الصبرة لعدم التفاوت فيها، وقطع ذراع من الثوب ضرر على البائع فلا يجوز أيضاً، كما لو باع جذعاً من سقف، وعندهما: يجوز في الكل، والدليل ما مر.(فتح، چلپی) ثوبا أو باع ثوبا مشاراً إليه يضره القطع. (ط)
ولو سمى الكل صح في الكُل، فلو نقص كيل أخذ بحصته أو فسخ، وإن زاد كيل فيما ذكرنا فللبائع، ولو نقص ذراع أخذ بكل الثمن أو ترك، وإن زاد فللمشتري.
ولو سمى الكل: أي كل المبيع والثمن في المجلس في هذه المسائل الثلاث - الصبرة والثلة والثوب – صح البيع سواء كان التسمية عند العقد أو بعده والحاصل أن شرط الجواز أحد الأمرين: إما العلم بجملة الثمن وإن لم يعلم عدد المعقود عليه، أو العلم بعدد المعقود عليه وإن لم يعلم جملة الثمن؛ لأن العلم بثمن كل واحد من الشياه أو الذرعان يغني عن التصريح بجملة الثمن، فلو قال: بعت منك هذه العشرة أغنام أو هذا الثوب وهو عشرة أذرع، أو قال بعت منك هذه الأغنام أو هذا الثوب بعشرة، كل شاة أو ذراع بدرهم، جاز اتفاقاً . (فتح) في الكل: أي في المسائل الثلاث؛ لزوال المانع. (ط) عيني)
نقص كيل: فيما لو اشترى صبرة على أنها مائة صاع بمائة درهم. (ط) أخذ بحصته إلخ : أي لو نقص كيل فيما إذا باع صبرة وسمى جملتها، ثم وجدها ناقصة، أخذ الباقي بحصته من الثمن؛ لأن الثمن ينقسم بالأجزاء على أجزاء المبيع المثلي مكيلاً أو موزوناً لا القيمي، أو فسخ البيع لفوات الصفة، وكذا كل مكيل أو موزون ليس في تبعيضه ضرر. (عيني، فتح) فللبائع أي فالزائد للبائع؛ لأنه لم يدخل في البيع إلا القدر المسمى، فبقي الزيادة على ملكه، والقدر ليس بوصف حتى يتبع الأصل. (عيني)
ذراع: فيما إذا باع مذروعا وسمى جملة الذرعان ولم يسم لكل ذراع ثمناً. (عيني) لأن الذراع وصف؛ لأنه عبارة عن الطول والعرض، والوصف لا يقابله شيء من الثمن كأطراف الحيوان. ثم اعلم أن المشايخ ذكروا في الفرق بين الأصل والوصف حدوداً، فقيل: إن ما يتعيب بالتبعيض والتشقيص، فالزيادة والنقصان فيه وصف، وما لا يتعيب فالزيادة والنقصان فيه أصل، وقيل: الوصف ما لوجوده تأثير في تقويم غيره، ولعدمه تأثير في نقصان غيره، والأصل ما لا يكون بهذه المثابة. وقيل: إن ما لا ينتقص قيمة الباقي بفواته فهو أصل وما ينتقص قيمة الباقي بفواته فهو وصف، فعلم في المكيلات والموزونات أصل والذراع في المذروعات وصف، فإذا انتقص قفيز من مائة قفيز لا يتعيب الباقي، ويشتري الباقي بحصته من الثمن، واليد والعين إذا فاتتا ينتقص قيمة النفس، فلا يشترى الباقي بالثمن الذي كان يشتري معه بحصته ما نقص، وكذا الذراع الواحد من الثوب أو الدار إذا فات، فيأخذ إن شاء بكل الثمن أو ترك. (كفاية، فتح) أو ترك والأصل فيه أن الذراع في المذروعات وصف والكيل في المكيلات أصل، فلا ينقسم الثمن على الأوصاف إلا عند التعيين، إلا أنه يثبت له الخيار لفوات الوصف المرغوب فيه. (عيني) فللمشتري: أي فهو للمشتري بذلك الثمن؛ لأن الذراع وصف لا يقابله شيء من الثمن. (ط، عيني)
And whoever sells a heap, each sa' by a dirham, it is valid for one sa'. And if he sells a flock or a cloth, each sheep or each cubit by a dirham, it is invalid in all, and by this fatwa is given. 'And if he specifies the total': meaning the total of the sold and the price in the session in these three cases – the heap, the flock, and the cloth – the sale is valid whether the specification is at the contract or after. The gist is that the condition of permissibility is one of two things: either knowledge of the total price even if the quantity of the object is unknown, or knowledge of the quantity of the object even if the total price is unknown; because knowledge of the price of each sheep or cubit suffices for stating the total price. For example, if he says 'I sold you these ten sheep' or 'this cloth which is ten cubits', or 'I sold you these sheep or this cloth for ten, each sheep or cubit for a dirham', it is valid by agreement. (Fath) 'In all' means in the three cases, due to the removal of the impediment. (T, Ayni) 'Shortage in measure' concerns when he bought a heap as one hundred sa' for one hundred dirhams. (T) 'He takes his portion etc.': meaning if there is a shortage in measure when he sold a heap and specified its total, then found it short, he takes the remaining by its portion of the price, because the price divides into parts over the parts of the sold item if it is mithli (fungible) by measure or weight, not qimi (non-fungible); or he cancels the sale due to loss of the desired attribute. Similarly for every weighed or measured item in whose division there is no harm. (Ayni, Fath) 'For the seller' means the excess is for the seller, because only the specified amount entered the sale, so the excess remains his property, and the amount is not a description to follow the origin. (Ayni) 'Cubit' concerns when he sells a measured-by-length item and specified the total cubits but did not specify a price for each cubit. (Ayni) Because the cubit is a description, as it expresses length and width, and the description is not compensated by any part of the price, like limbs of an animal. Then know that the scholars mentioned definitions for the difference between origin and description. Some said: what is damaged by division and partition, increase and decrease in it is a description, and what is not damaged, increase and decrease in it is an origin. Others said: the description is that whose existence affects the valuation of others and whose absence affects the deficiency of others, and the origin is not like that. Others said: what does not diminish the value of the remainder by its loss is an origin, and what diminishes the value of the remainder by its loss is a description. Thus it is known that in measured and weighed items, the standard is an origin, and the cubit in length-measured items is a description. So if a qafiz is missing from a hundred qafiz, the remainder is not defective, and the remainder is bought with its portion of the price. But if a hand or eye is lost, the value of the self diminishes, so the remainder is not bought with the portion that would have been the price for what was lost. Similarly, if one cubit of a cloth or house is lost, he takes the entire price or leaves. (Kifaya, Fath) And the origin is that the cubit in length-measured items is a description and the measure in measured items is an origin, so the price does not divide over descriptions unless specified, but he has the option due to the loss of the desired attribute. (Ayni) 'For the buyer' means it is for the buyer with that price, because the cubit is a description that is not compensated by any part of the price. (T, Ayni)
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage covers rules for selling items per unit (each sa', each sheep, each cubit) and the consequences of shortfall or excess. The matn states: selling a heap (subrah) 'each sa' by a dirham' is valid only for one sa' according to Abu Hanifa; selling a flock (thallah) each sheep or a cloth each cubit is invalid in all. The fatwa is given by the latter. The commentary details the intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa argues that the price of the remaining units is unknown, corrupting the contract, and analogy to selling cloth by its number supports his view. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say the sale is valid in all because the object is known by pointing, and ignorance can be removed by measuring in the session; they also analogize to the permissibility of jizaf. The fatwa follows the Sahibayn for ease. For the flock and cloth, Abu Hanifa rules total invalidity because of variation in value and harm from cutting; the Sahibayn allow all with the same reasoning. If the total is specified (e.g., ten sheep for ten dirhams), the sale is valid by agreement. Then the commentary turns to shortfall and excess: for measured (makil/mawzun) goods, if the actual amount falls short, the buyer takes the remainder with a proportional price or cancels; if excess, the seller keeps it. For length-measured (madhru') goods like cloth, if short, the buyer takes the entire cloth at full price or cancels; if excess, the buyer gets it free because the cubit is a description, not an origin. The scholars define 'asl' (origin) as what does not diminish the value of the remainder when missing, and 'wasf' (description) as what does diminish it. Applied: measure in grain is asl, cubit in cloth is wasf.

Key Terms
أصل (aṣl): The standard unit (e.g., measure for grain) such that loss does not defect the remainder.
وصف (waṣf): A description or attribute (e.g., cubit for cloth) such that loss defects the remainder.
مثلي (mithlī): Fungible goods (homogeneous, measurable by weight/volume).
قيمي (qīmī): Non-fungible goods (unique, not homogeneous).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a cloth specified as 10 cubits for 10 dirhams is found to be 9 cubits, what are the buyer's options under Hanafi law?
A) Pay 9 dirhams and take 9 cubits
B) Pay 10 dirhams and take 9 cubits, or cancel
C) Pay 10 dirhams and take 10 cubits (seller must add 1 cubit)
D) The contract is void

Key Takeaway
The asl-wasf distinction determines how shortfall/excess is handled: proportional for origins, full-price-or-cancel for descriptions.

Asl vs Wasf: Prorating and Options in Sales Deficiencies
Ruling and commentary on asl vs wasf in sales

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for deficiency and increase in measured and length-measured goods, and apply the asl/wasf distinction to determine whether the price is prorated or the buyer has an option.

Core Idea
Deficiency in a measured good is prorated; deficiency in a length-measured good gives the buyer an option due to the asl/wasf distinction.

When a sold item is found deficient or excessive, Hanafi law treats measured/weighed goods differently from length-measured goods. The key is whether the deficient part is an original part (asl) or a description (wasf). This lesson unpacks the ruling and the underlying definitions so you can apply the correct remedy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of goods
Classify the sold item as either makil/mawzun (measured/weighed) or madhrur (length-measured). This determines whether the deficiency is treated as asl or wasf.
Makilat include grains, liquids; madhrurat include cloth, land.
2
State the ruling for deficiency
For makilat: buyer takes the remainder at its proportionate share of the price or cancels. For madhrurat: buyer takes the deficient item at the full price or cancels.
The option is the buyer's, not the seller's.
3
State the ruling for increase
For makilat: the excess belongs to the seller. For madhrurat: the excess belongs to the buyer at no extra cost.
This follows from the asl/wasf logic.
4
Understand the asl/wasf definitions
Asl: a part whose loss does not diminish the value of the remainder. Wasf: a part whose loss reduces the value of the remainder. The cubit is wasf; a measure of grain is asl.
The definitions are based on harm from division and effect on valuation.
5
Apply the distinction to new cases
Given any good, assess whether splitting it would harm the remainder. If yes, it is wasf; if no, it is asl. Then apply the appropriate ruling.
Use the three criteria from the mashayikh: harm from division, effect on valuation of others, and effect on value of remainder.

Source Text

(عيني) أن القدر ذراع فيما إذا باع مذروعا وسمى جملة الذرعان ولم يسم لكل ذراع ثمنا . (عيني) لأن الذراع وصف؛ لأنه عبارة عن الطول والعرض، والوصف لا يقابله شيء من الثمن كأطراف الحيوان. ثم اعلم أن المشايخ ذكروا في الفرق بين الأصل والوصف حدوداً، فقيل: إن ما يتعيب بالتبعيض والتشقيص، فالزيادة والنقصان فيه وصف، وما لا يتعيب فالزيادة والنقصان فيه أصل، وقيل: الوصف ما لوجوده تأثير في تقويم غيره، ولعدمه تأثير في نقصان غيره، والأصل ما لا يكون بهذه المثابة. وقيل: إن ما لا ينتقص قيمة الباقي بفواته فهو أصل وما ينتقص قيمة الباقي بفواته فهو وصف، فعلم في المكيلات والموزونات أصل والذراع في المذروعات وصف، فإذا انتقص قفيز من مائة قفيز لا يتعيب الباقي، ويشتري الباقي بحصته من الثمن، واليد والعين إذا فاتتا ينتقص قيمة النفس، فلا يشترى الباقي بالثمن الذي كان يشتري معه بحصته ما نقص، وكذا الذراع الواحد من الثوب أو الدار إذا فات، فيأخذ إن شاء بكل الثمن أو ترك. Source pages p. 254

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq states the ruling on sales where the total quantity of the object is specified (samma al-kull) but not the unit price. The commentator expands on the distinction between measured/weighed goods (makilat/mawzunat) and length-measured goods (madhrurat). In measured goods (e.g., grain), a deficiency is handled by prorating the price: the buyer takes the remaining quantity at its proportionate share of the price, or cancels the sale. An excess belongs to the seller because only the specified amount was sold. In length-measured goods (e.g., cloth, land), a deficiency gives the buyer the option to take the entire deficient item at the full price or cancel, because the cubit is considered a description (wasf) of the item, not an independent original part (asl). An excess belongs to the buyer at no extra cost. The commentator then defines the difference between asl and wasf according to the late scholars (mashayikh): (1) an asl is not harmed by division, while a wasf is harmed; (2) a wasf affects the valuation of others, an asl does not; (3) loss of a wasf reduces the value of the remainder, loss of an asl does not. For example, if one qafiz is missing from a heap of grain, the remaining 99 qafiz are not defective and can be taken at 99/100 of the price. But if a cubit is missing from a cloth, the remaining cloth is worth less, so the buyer may take it at full price or cancel. The ruling that the seller has no option when the cubit increases is also noted; the buyer benefits from the increase. Any ambiguity in the phrase 'البائع إن شاء الفوات الوصف المرغوب فيه' does not affect the clear ruling.

Key Terms
الأصل (al-asl): The original substance or part of a sold item, whose loss does not diminish the value of the remainder proportionately; e.g., a measure of grain.
الوصف (al-wasf): An attribute or part whose loss degrades the remainder's value, such as a cubit of length in cloth; it does not have a separate share of the price.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He may take the cloth at 9/10 of the price or cancel.
B) He may take the cloth at the full price or cancel.
C) He may only cancel the sale.
D) He must take the cloth at the reduced price.

Key Takeaway
The classification of an item as asl or wasf determines whether a deficiency is prorated or gives an option; similarly, an excess belongs to the seller for asl and to the buyer for wasf.

Buyer's Options with Per-Cubit Pricing
Ruling on per-cubit sale with deficiency or excess

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the buyer's options when the seller specifies a per-cubit price and the total length is deficient or excessive, and explain the legal reasoning based on whether the cubit is treated as an original or a description.

Core Idea
When each cubit has its own price, it becomes an independent item — deficiency allows prorated take or cancel; excess allows full take or cancel.

In a sale where the price is set per cubit, each cubit is treated as an independent original (asl), not merely a description. This affects the buyer's remedies if the actual length differs from what was stated. Understanding this distinction is essential for determining the validity of partial acceptance and the scope of the buyer's choice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the pricing structure
The seller says 'each cubit for such-and-such' (e.g., each cubit for 1 dirham). This makes the cubit an independent unit of sale.
Compare with total-price scenario where the price is for the whole length without per-unit breakdown.
2
Analyze deficiency
If the actual length is less than stated (e.g., specified 10 cubits but only 9 present), the buyer may take the actual length at the prorated price (9 dirhams) or cancel the sale entirely. He cannot insist on the full length at full price because the specified quantity was not delivered.
The buyer has an additional option due to 'tafarruq al-safqah' (division of the contract) — taking partial delivery is permitted because each cubit is an independent item.
3
Analyze excess
If the actual length exceeds the stated amount (e.g., 11 cubits instead of 10), the buyer may accept the entire extra length at the increased price (11 dirhams) or cancel. He may not take only the specified 10 cubits and leave the extra, because splitting the length-measured item harms the seller (unlike a divisible heap of grain).
The option is given because the increase, though beneficial, is mixed with the harm of higher total price.
4
Understand the underlying rationale
In per-cubit pricing, the cubit is an 'asl' (original), not a mere 'wasf' (description). This is because it is given a separate price and is a physical entity that can be benefited from independently. As an asl, it can be the subject of partial delivery or rejection.
This contrasts with the total-price scenario where the length is a description of a single item, so deficiency voids the entire contract.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو قال: كلّ ذراع بكذا ونقص أخذ بحصته أو ترك، وإن زاد أخذ كله كل ذراع بكذا أو فسخ، وفسد بيع إنما قال في الأولى أو ترك، وفي الثانية أو فسخ؛ لأن المسمى لما كان في الأولى، لم يوجد المبيع، فلم ينعقد البيع حقيقة، فكان أخذ الأقل بالأقل كالبيع بالتعاطي، وفي الثانية وجد المبيع مع زيادة هي أصل لا وصف؛ لأن الذراع وإن كان وصفاً يصلح أن يكون أصلا؛ لأنه عين ينتفع به بانفراده، فإذا سمي جعل أصلا، فإذا صار أصلا فوجده ناقصا أخذه بحصته، ويثبت له الخيار؛ لتفرق الصفقة عليه، وإن وجده زائداً فهو بالخيار في الأخذ والفسخ؛ لأن زيادة المبيع وإن كانت نفعاً لكن يشوبها ضرر زيادة الثمن فيتخير وليس له أن يأخذ القدر المسمى ويترك الزائد؛ لأن التبعيض يضره، بخلاف الصبرة، ألا ترى أنه لا يجوز بيع بعض المذروع ابتداء وفي الصبرة يجوز. (فتح)
And if he said: each cubit for such-and-such, and it decreased, he takes according to his share or leaves, and if it increased, he takes all of it, each cubit for such-and-such, or cancels. And the sale is invalid. He only said in the first: 'or leaves', and in the second: 'or cancels'; because when the named was in the first, the sold item was not found, so the sale did not actually contract, so taking the lesser for the lesser was like a sale by mutual exchange. And in the second, the sold item was found with an increase that is original, not description; because the cubit, even though it is a description, is suitable to be an original because it is a physical entity that can be benefited from independently. So when specified, it is made an original. So when it becomes an original and he finds it deficient, he takes it by his share, and he has the option due to the division of the contract upon him. And if he finds it increased, he has the option to take or cancel, because the increase of the sold item, although beneficial, is mixed with harm of increased price, so he has choice. And he may not take the specified amount and leave the excess, because division harms him, unlike the heap. Do you not see that it is not permissible to sell part of a length-measured item initially, while in a heap it is permissible? (Fath)
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage discusses a different scenario: when the seller explicitly sets a per-unit price for each cubit (e.g., 'each cubit for one dirham'). Now, the cubit is treated as an original (asl) because it is specified with a separate price. The commentator explains why the ruling differs from the previous case. If the total length is stated (e.g., '10 cubits for 10 dirhams') and it falls short, the buyer may take it at full price or cancel, because the cubit is a description. But if per-cubit price is stated, the cubit becomes an asl. So if the total length is deficient (e.g., seller says 'each cubit for a dirham' implying 10 cubits, but only 9 are found), the buyer may take the 9 cubits at 9 dirhams (prorated) or cancel, because the cubit is now an asl subject to division. If the length exceeds (e.g., 11 cubits found), the buyer has an option to take the whole 11 cubits at 11 dirhams or cancel, but may not take only 10 cubits and leave the extra, because splitting the length-measured item harms the seller (unlike a heap of grain which is divisible). The commentator also clarifies the wording: for deficiency, the option is 'take or leave' (the item at full price? Actually confusion: in the first scenario of total price, the text says 'أخذ بكل الثمن أو ترك' meaning take at full price or cancel; for per-unit price, it says 'أخذ بحصته أو ترك' meaning take at prorated share or cancel. The comment explains that in the first scenario, the sale was invalid due to non-existence of the sold item? Actually it says 'لم يوجد المبيع' meaning the specified item (10 cubits) was not found, so the contract was not valid, and taking the lesser at lesser price is like a new transaction by taking mutual exchange (ta'ati). In the second scenario, the specified item is found with an increase, and the cubit has become an asl, so the buyer may prorate.

Key Terms
التعاطي (al-ta'ati): A form of sale by mutual exchange of goods without formal offer and acceptance, considered valid for small transactions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He may take the 11 cubits at 22 dirhams or cancel.
B) He may take only 10 cubits at 20 dirhams and leave the extra.
C) He must take the whole cloth at 20 dirhams.
D) He may take the 11 cubits at 20 dirhams.

Key Takeaway
When a price is per cubit, each cubit is an independent item: deficiency allows prorated purchase or cancel; excess allows full purchase at higher price or cancel.

Selling 'Ten Cubits of a House': A Hanafi Dispute on Specificity vs. Sharing
Intra-Hanafi dispute on sale of a measured length

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Abu Hanifa's ruling on selling a measured length of a house, explain the Sahibayn's counterargument using qiyas, and distinguish between dhira' (specific length) and sahm (undivided share).

Core Idea
A sale of a measured length requires location specification; a sale of an undivided share does not.

In Hanafi sales law, the distinction between selling a specific portion of a property and selling an undivided share can determine the contract's validity. This lesson examines a classical intra-Hanafi dispute: is it valid to sell 'ten cubits of this house'? Abu Hanifa says no, the Sahibayn say yes. Their disagreement hinges on the nature of the term 'cubit' versus 'share', and the risk of dispute due to unknown location.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
State Abu Hanifa's ruling (invalid) and the Sahibayn's ruling (valid). Note that the three other imams (Shafi'i, Malik, Ahmad) side with the Sahibayn.
This is a rare case where Abu Hanifa is stricter than his students.
2
Understand the Sahibayn's qiyas
The Sahibayn analogize: ten cubits from a hundred cubits is one-tenth, just like ten shares from a hundred shares. Since selling ten shares is valid (undivided portion), selling ten cubits should also be valid.
Their analogy relies on the numerical proportion being the same.
3
Analyze Abu Hanifa's response
Abu Hanifa distinguishes: 'cubit' (dhira') refers to a specific measured piece, not an undivided share. A real cubit must be localized; unknown location leads to dispute over value (different parts of a house have different values). Therefore, the contract is void for jahalah mufdiyah ila al-niza'.
The distinction hinges on the linguistic origin: dhira' is a measuring stick; sahm is inherently undivided.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: under Abu Hanifa the sale is fasid (invalid) and must be rescinded; under the Sahibayn the sale is sahih (valid) and binding.
No mufta bihi is stated in this passage; the commentator leans toward Abu Hanifa.

Source Text

وفسد بيع إلخ: عند أبي حنيفة، وقالا: يجوز؛ لأن عشرة أذرع من مائة ذراع عشرها، فأشبه عشرة أسهم من مائة أسهم، وبه قالت الثلاثة وله أن البيع وقع على قدر معين من الدار لا على شائع؛ لأن الذراع في الأصل اسم للخشبة يذرع بها واستعير ههنا لما يحله وهو معين لا مشاع، والمشاع لا يتصور أن يذرع، فإذا أريد به ما يحله وهو معين، لكنه مجهول الموضع أي لم يعين ذلك الموضع أنه من مقدم الدار أو من مؤخرها، وجوانبها تتفاوت قيمة فكان المعقود عليه مجهولا جهالة مفضية إلى النزاع، فيفسد كبيع بيت من بيوت الدار، بخلاف السهم؛ فإنه اسم للشائع الغير المعين فافترقا، فلا يفسد بيع عشرة أسهم من دار أو حمام؛ لأن عشرة أسهم شائع =
And the sale is invalid etc.: according to Abu Hanifa, and they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: it is valid, because ten cubits from a hundred cubits are a tenth of it, thus resembling ten shares from a hundred shares, and the three (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad? Actually 'the three' likely means Al-Shafi'i, Malik, and Ahmad? The text says 'وبها قالت الثلاثة' meaning the three [imams] said it, but context suggests it's the Sahibayn plus others) and he (Abu Hanifa) has the argument that the sale occurred on a specific measure of the house, not on a share, because the term 'cubit' originally is the name of the stick used for measuring, and is used metaphorically here for what it measures, which is specific, not shared, and the shared cannot be imagined to be measured. So when by it is meant what it measures, which is specific but unknown in location—meaning that location was not specified whether from the front of the house or the back, and its sides differ in value—so the subject matter was unknown with an ignorance leading to dispute, thus it is invalid, like the sale of a room from the rooms of a house. Unlike the 'share' (sahm), because it is a name for the unspecified undivided portion, so they differ. Thus the sale of ten shares in a house or a bathhouse is not invalid, because ten shares are undivided.
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute about selling a specified quantity of a length-measured property like a house. For example, selling 'ten cubits of this house'. Abu Hanifa rules the sale invalid (fasid) because the exact location of those ten cubits is unknown—front, back, or side of the house vary in value, leading to potential dispute. The subject matter is therefore unknown in a way that causes conflict. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argue it is valid, analogizing to selling ten shares (sahm) of a house, which is valid because ten shares are an undivided portion (shai'). The difference, according to Abu Hanifa, is that 'cubit' (dhira') originally refers to the measuring stick, then metaphorically to the measured length, which must be a specific, identifiable piece. Since it cannot be undivided (musha'), it requires localization. 'Share' (sahm) inherently means an undivided portion, so selling ten shares is valid. The commentator also notes that the three other imams (likely al-Shafi'i, Malik, and Ahmad) agree with the Sahibayn on validity. This dispute highlights the Hanafi emphasis on avoiding gharar (uncertainty) in contracts.

Key Terms
الذراع (al-dhira'): A unit of length, originally the measuring stick; metaphorically the measured length. Here it denotes a specific, localized portion of a property.
السهم (al-sahm): An undivided share or portion of a property, e.g., one share in a jointly owned house. It is musha' (undivided) by definition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does Abu Hanifa rule the sale of 'ten cubits of a house' invalid?
A) Because it is impossible to measure cubits in a house.
B) Because the location of the ten cubits is unknown, causing potential dispute.
C) Because the price is uncertain.
D) Because the sale of shares is not allowed.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi sales law, selling a measured length requires specification of its location to avoid invalidating gharar; selling an undivided share does not.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Ruling on Buying by Cubits with Shortage or Excess
States ruling for cubit-measured sales with khiyar and distinguishes from measured/weighed goods

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a cubit-measured item is found shorter or longer than specified, distinguish between cubit as description and measure/weight as essence, and identify the intra-Hanafi dispute on selling specific cubits from a larger property.

Core Idea
In cubit sales, the buyer has an option if the length differs; the cubit is a description, not the essence—unlike measure and weight.

This lesson unpacks a key distinction in Hanafi sales law: the difference between goods sold by length (dhiray) and those sold by measure or weight. The passage from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq explains the option rights when the actual length differs, and how this leads to several subsidiary rulings. It also addresses a disagreement among the Hanafi masters regarding the sale of a specific number of cubits from a larger property.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the basic rule
The passage describes a buyer who purchases an item described as a specific number of cubits for a total price, or per cubit. State the ruling when the item is shorter or longer.
Focus on the buyer's option (khiyar) and the seller's lack of option when there is excess.
2
Understand the legal basis: cubit as description (wasf)
Explain why the buyer has an option: the cubit specification is a description, so a deviation gives an option, unlike measure/weight which are the essence.
The passage uses the analogy of buying a defective pound and finding it sound.
3
Contrast with measured/weighed goods
List the three subsidiary distinctions: disposal before measurement, permissibility of selling one for two, and the dispute on selling specific cubits.
These highlight the practical consequences of the wasf/asl distinction.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
Compare Abu Hanifa's position (sale of ten cubits from a hundred-cubit house is fasid) with the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (valid), and note the mufta bihi position.
The dispute centers on whether the cubit refers to a specific portion (causing jahalah) or an undivided share.

Source Text

ما يتعلق بالبيع البائع إن شاء الفوات الوصف المرغوب فيه ولا خيار للبائع، ولو قال: كلّ ذراع بكذا ونقص أخذ بحصته أو ترك، وإن زاد أخذ كله كل ذراع بكذا أو فسخ، وفسد بيع ولا خيار إلخ أي إن اشترى ثوباً أو أرضاً أو داراً على أنه عشرة أذرع بعشرة، فوجدها أقل، فالمشتري بالخيار، إن شاء أخذه بجملة الثمن، وإن شاء ترك، وإن وجدها أكثر من الذراع الذي سماه، فهو للمشتري ولا خيار للبائع كما إذا شرح رط معيباً فوجده سليماً، وتظهر ثمرة كون الذراع وصفاً والقدر – أي الكيل والوزن – أصلاً في مواضع منها هذه المسألة ومنها: أنه لا يجوز للمشتري التصرف في المكيل والموزون قبل الكيل أو الوزن إذا اشتراه بشرط ذلك، ويجوز له في المذروع قبل الذرع؛ لأن الذرع لما كان وصفاً لم يلزم اختلاط المبيع بغيره، والكيل والوزن أصل فيلزم الاختلاط إذا زاد المبيع؛ لأن الزائد للبائع، ومنها: أن بيع الواحد بالاثنين لا يجوز في المكيلات والموزونات، فلا يجوز البيع بدون المساواة، بخلاف المذروع. (فتح) كل ذراع بكذا: بأن قال: بعتكه على أنه عشرة أذرع كل ذراع بدرهم مثلا. (عيني) أخذ بحصته: أي فالمشتري بالخيار إن شاء أخذ الموجود. (ط) وإن زاد ذراع فللمشتري الخيار إن شاء. بكذا: أي بدرهم مثلا بمثل ما قال في الأول. (عيني) أو فسخ أي البيع؛ لأن الذراع وإن كان وصفاً، لكنه صار أصلا بالتعيين كما ذكرنا، وثبوت الخيار للمشتري لتفرق الصفقة عليه. [رمز الحقائق: ٦/٢] إنما قال في الأولى أو ترك، وفي الثانية أو فسخ؛ لأن المسمى لما كان في الأولى، لم يوجد المبيع، فلم ينعقد البيع حقيقة، فكان أخذ الأقل بالأقل كالبيع بالتعاطي، وفي الثانية وجد المبيع مع زيادة هي أصل لا وصف؛ لأن الذراع وإن كان وصفاً يصلح أن يكون أصلا؛ لأنه عين ينتفع به ناقصاً لكل ذراع [همنا؟] جعل أصلا، بانفراده، فإذا سمي فإذا صار أصلا فوجده ناقصا أخذه بحصته، ويثبت له الخيار؛ لتفرق الصفقة عليه، وإن وجده زائداً فهو بالخيار في الأخذ والفسخ؛ لأن زيادة المبيع وإن كانت نفعاً لكن يشوبها ضرر زيادة الثمن فيتخير وليس له أن يأخذ القدر المسمى ويترك الزائد؛ لأن التبعيض يضره، بخلاف الصبرة، ألا ترى أنه لا يجوز بيع بعض المذروع ابتداء وفي الصبرة يجوز. (فتح) وفسد بيع إلخ: عند أبي حنيفة، وقالا: يجوز؛ لأن عشرة أذرع من مائة ذراع عشرها، فأشبه عشرة أسهم من مائة أسهم، وبه قالت الثلاثة وله أن البيع وقع على قدر معين من الدار لا على شائع؛ لأن الذراع في الأصل اسم للخشبة يذرع بها واستعير ههنا لما يحله وهو معين لا مشاع، والمشاع لا يتصور أن يذرع، فإذا أريد به ما يحله وهو معين، لكنه مجهول الموضع أي لم يعين ذلك الموضع أنه من مقدم الدار أو من مؤخرها، وجوانبها تتفاوت قيمة فكان المعقود عليه مجهولا جهالة مفضية إلى النزاع، فيفسد كبيع بيت من بيوت الدار، بخلاف السهم؛ فإنه اسم للشائع الغير المعين فافترقا، فلا يفسد بيع عشرة أسهم من دار أو حمام؛ لأن عشرة أسهم شائع = عشرة أذرع من دار لا أسهم، بل كان صاحب عشرة أسهم شريكا لصاحب تسعة أسهم في جميع الدار على قدر نصيبهما منها، وليس لصاحب الكثير أن يدفع إلى صاحب القليل قدر نصيبه في أي موضع كان فلا يؤدي إلى المنازعة. (عيني، فتح، كفاية) من مائة سهم لا أسهم: أي لا يفسد بيع عشرة أسهم . بالإجماع؛ لشيوع السهم لا الذراع (عيني)
Related to sales: The seller - if he wishes the loss of the desired description - and there is no option for the seller. And if he said: each cubit for such amount, and it is short, he takes at its share or leaves; and if it increases, he takes all of it, each cubit for such amount, or he cancels, and the sale is corrupt. 'And no option' etc. meaning if he bought a garment or land or a house on the basis that it is ten cubits for ten, and he found it less, then the buyer has the option: if he wishes he takes it for the total price, and if he wishes he leaves. And if he found it more than the cubit he named, then it is for the buyer and there is no option for the seller, just as if he bought a pound of defective [goods] and found it sound. And the fruit of making the cubit a description and the capacity - i.e. measure and weight - a basis appears in places, including this issue and: that it is not permissible for the buyer to dispose of measured and weighed [goods] before measurement or weight if he bought it with that condition, and it is permissible for him in the measured cubit before cubit-measurement; because the cubit-measurement since it is a description, no mixing of the sold item with others occurs, while measure and weight are a basis so mixing occurs if the sold item increases, because the excess is for the seller. And including: that selling one for two is not permissible in measured and weighed items, so selling without equality is not permissible, unlike the cubit-measured. (Fath) 'each cubit for such amount': i.e. he said: I sold it to you on the basis that it is ten cubits, each cubit for a dirham for example. ('Inayah) 'he takes at its share': meaning the buyer has the option: if he wishes he takes what exists. (T) 'and if a cubit increases': then the buyer has the option if he wishes. 'for such amount': i.e. for a dirham for example, like what he said in the first. ('Inayah) 'or he cancels': i.e. the sale; because the cubit, even though it is a description, became a basis by specification as we mentioned, and the establishment of the option for the buyer is due to the splitting of the transaction upon him. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 6/2] He said in the first 'or leaves', and in the second 'or cancels'; because the named [amount] in the first, the sold item was not found, so the sale was not actually concluded, so taking the lesser for the lesser is like a sale by mutual giving; while in the second, the sold item was found with an increase that is a basis not a description; because the cubit, although it was a description, is suitable to be a basis because it is a substance from which one benefits... deficient? for each cubit [?] made as a basis, individually, so if he named it and it became a basis and he found it deficient, he takes it at its share, and the option is established for him due to the splitting of the transaction upon him. And if he found it increased, then he has the option to take or cancel; because the increase of the sold item, although it is a benefit, is mixed with the harm of increase in price, so he has an option. And he does not have the right to take the named amount and leave the excess, because partiality harms him, unlike the heap; do you not see that it is not permissible to sell some of the cubit-measured [item] initially, but in the heap it is permissible. (Fath) 'and the sale is corrupt' etc.: according to Abu Hanifa, and the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: it is permissible; because ten cubits from a hundred cubits are a tenth, so it resembles ten shares from a hundred shares, and this is the view of the three. And he has [the argument] that the sale occurred on a specific amount of the house, not on an undivided share; because the cubit originally is the name for the stick with which one measures, and is used metaphorically here for what it measures, which is specific and not undivided, and the undivided cannot be imagined to be measured. So if what it measures is intended, and it is specific but its location is unknown, i.e. that location was not specified as from the front of the house or its back, and its sides differ in value, so the object of contract is unknown with an ignorance leading to dispute, so it is corrupt like the sale of a room from the rooms of the house, unlike the share; for it is the name for the undivided unspecified, so they differ, and the sale of ten shares from a house or a bathhouse is not corrupt, because ten shares are undivided = ten cubits from a house not shares, but rather the owner of ten shares becomes a partner with the owner of nine shares in the entire house according to the share of each, and the one with many cannot give the one with few his share in any location, so it does not lead to dispute. ('Inayah, Fath, Kifayah) 'from a hundred shares not shares': meaning the sale of ten shares is not corrupt by consensus, due to the commonality of the share, not the cubit. ('Inayah)
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It begins by stating the general principle: when a buyer purchases a cubit-measured item (like cloth, land, or a house) with a specified total length (e.g., ten cubits for ten dirhams), and it turns out to be shorter, the buyer has an option (khiyar): he may take it at the full price or cancel. If it is longer, the excess belongs to the buyer without any option for the seller. The key legal distinction is that the cubit (dhira') is considered a description (wasf), whereas measure (kayl) and weight (wazn) are considered the essence (asl) of the thing sold. This difference yields several subsidiary rulings: (1) In measured/weighed goods, the buyer cannot dispose of them before weighing/measuring because the exact quantity is essential, but in cubit-measured goods, he can dispose before measuring because the cubit is merely descriptive. (2) Selling one of measured/weighed goods for two of the same kind (without equality) is invalid, but it is allowed in cubit-measured goods. The commentary then details the case where the price is set per cubit (each cubit for a dirham). Here, if there is a shortage, the buyer takes what exists at its proportionate price and has an option; if there is an excess, he takes all at the total price or cancels. The difference between the two formulations is explained: in the first (total price), the sale was not truly concluded for the missing portion, so taking the lesser for the lesser is like a sale by mutual giving; in the second (per cubit price), the sale includes the excess which is a basis, so he must take all or cancel. The commentary also discusses the case of selling a specific number of cubits from a larger property (e.g., ten cubits from a hundred-cubit house). Abu Hanifa rules this sale corrupt (fasid) because the cubit refers to a specific but unlocated portion, leading to ignorance (jahalah) that causes dispute. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad rule it valid, comparing it to selling shares (as-hum), which are undivided and thus not subject to the same ignorance. The final part emphasizes that selling ten shares of a house is valid by consensus because shares are common and undivided. The authority weight of the rulings: The main ruling on khiyar and the distinction between wasf and asl is from Zahir al-Riwayah. The dispute on selling specific number of cubits is also from Zahir al-Riwayah, with the mufta bihi position being that of Abu Hanifa (fasid) due to jahalah, as supported by the majority of later scholars.

Key Terms
الذراع (al-dhira'): A unit of length, but legally treated as a description (wasf) in sales, not the essence (asl) of the good.
الكيل والوزن (al-kayl wa al-wazn): Measure and weight; these are considered the essence (asl) of the goods in sales, so any discrepancy in them affects the validity of the contract.
خيار (khiyar): The right of an option given to the buyer (or seller) to confirm or cancel the sale due to a defect or discrepancy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if someone buys a piece of cloth on the basis that it is ten cubits for ten dirhams, and it turns out to be eleven cubits, what is the ruling?
A) The seller has the option to cancel the sale.
B) The buyer takes the cloth for ten dirhams and has no option.
C) The buyer may take it for ten dirhams or cancel.
D) The sale is invalid due to gharar.

Key Takeaway
In cubit sales, the buyer has an option for shortage or excess; the cubit is a description, while measure/weight are the essence, leading to different rules.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Buying a Bundle: Shortage, Excess, and Price Clarity
Ruling on bundle sale with count variance and price clarity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on buying a bundle of cloths when the count is short or excessive, distinguishing between total price and per-unit pricing.

Core Idea
A bundle sale is corrupt unless each item's price is fixed; then shortage gives the buyer a valid option.

When buying a bundle of cloths, the exact number must be certain to avoid disputes. The Hanafi school distinguishes between pricing the whole bundle and pricing each cloth individually. This passage explains when the sale is valid, when it is corrupt, and what options the buyer has.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Initial Ruling
The act is buying a bundle of cloths on the basis that it contains a specified number of cloths. The matn states that if the actual count is short or excessive, the sale is corrupt (fasid).
This is the default ruling when no per-unit price is mentioned.
2
Examine the Exception: Per-Unit Pricing
If the seller specifies a price for each cloth (e.g., each cloth for a dirham), then if the count is short, the sale is valid for the present cloths proportionally, and the buyer has an option (khiyar) to take or leave. If the count exceeds, the sale is still corrupt.
The rationale: per-unit pricing removes ignorance (jahalah) of the price for each item.
3
Analyze the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
A narration from Abu Hanifa states that even with per-unit pricing, the sale is corrupt because it combines existing and non-existing items in one contract. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold it is valid. The preferred view (sahih) is validity with khiyar.
The later scholars (al-Nahr, Fath) reject the narration from Abu Hanifa as weak.
4
Understand the Reason (Ta'lil)
When total price is given without per-unit pricing, in case of shortage the price per cloth is unknown (jahalah al-thaman), and in case of excess, the identity of the extra cloth is unknown (jahalah al-mabi'). Both lead to disputes.
Cloths are qimi goods; their parts cannot be proportionally divided on the total price.
5
Apply the Ruling to a New Scenario
Suppose someone buys a bundle of cloths at a total price of 100 dinars for 10 cloths, but finds only 8. The sale is corrupt. If the price was 10 dinars per cloth, the sale is valid for 8 cloths at 80 dinars, with the buyer having the option to cancel.
This illustrates the practical consequence of the rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو اشترى عدلاً على أنه عشرة أثواب فنقص أو [من مائة ذراع أو من حمام؟] زاد فسد، ولو بين لكل ثوب ثمناً ونقص صح بقدره وخير، وإن زاد فسد، ومن [أي ثوب على العشرة البائع؟] ثوب من المسمى البيع اشترى ثوباً على أنه عشرة أذرع كل ذراع بدرهم أخذه بعشرة أخذ المشتري الثوب دارهم ثوب على المسمى في الكل فلم يلزم فيه جهالة تفضي إلى المنازعة. (عيني، فتح، كفاية) ثم: عشرة أثواب بعشرة دنانير مثلا، فلم يبين ثمن كل ثوب (عيني) فسد أي البيع؛ لجهالة الثمن في النقصان؛ لأنه لا ينقسم أجزاؤه على أجزاء القيمي، ولجهالة المبيع في فصل الزيادة؛ لأنه يحتاج إلى رد الزائد، فيتنازعان في الثوب المردود. (فتح) ثوب ثمنا بأن قال: بعتك هذا العدل على أنه عشرة أثواب كل ثوب بدرهم. (مسكين) صح بقدره أي بقدر الموجود؛ لأن ثمن كل واحد من الثياب معلوم، فالموجود يصح فيه البيع، ويبطل في المعدوم، وعن أبي حنيفة: أنه يفسد؛ لأن البائع جمع بين معدوم وموجود في صفقة واحدة. [رمز الحقائق: ٦/٢] والصحيح أنه يجوز في فصل النقصان عندهم جميعاً؛ لأنه لم يجعل قبول العقد في المعدوم شرطاً لقبوله في الموجود، بل قصد بيع الموجود إلا أنه غلط في العدد، وفي النهر [٣٥٣/٣] جعل الفساد في النقصان رواية عن أبي حنيفة فيه نظر، بل هو لبعض المشايخ وليس بصحيح. (فتح) وخير: أي المشتري إن شاء أخذ الباقي بحصته من الثمن، وإن شاء ترك لتفرق الصفقة. (مسكين، ط) فسد: البيع في الكل؛ لجهالة الزائد فتؤدي إلى المنازعة. (ط)
And if he bought a bundle on the basis that it is ten cloths, and it is short or [from a hundred cubits or from a bath?] it increases, it is corrupt; and if he stated a price for each cloth and it is short, it is valid for its amount and he has an option, and if it increases, it is corrupt; and from [any cloth on the ten the seller?] a cloth from the named sale he bought a cloth on the basis that it is ten cubits each cubit for a dirham, he takes it for ten, the buyer takes the cloth for dirhams, a cloth on the named in all, so no ignorance leading to dispute arises. ('Inayah, Fath, Kifayah) Then: ten cloths for ten dinars for example, and he did not specify the price of each cloth ('Inayah), it is corrupt, i.e. the sale; due to ignorance of the price in case of shortage, because its parts cannot be divided upon the parts of the value goods, and due to ignorance of the sold item in case of increase, because he needs to return the excess, so they will dispute about the returned cloth. (Fath) A cloth with a price, i.e. he said: I sold you this bundle on the basis that it is ten cloths, each cloth for a dirham. (Miskin) It is valid for its amount, i.e. for the amount present; because the price of each cloth is known, so the sale is valid for the present and void for the absent. And from Abu Hanifa: that it is corrupt; because the seller combined absent and present in one transaction. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 6/2] And the correct view is that it is permissible in the case of shortage according to all of them; because he did not make acceptance of the contract for the absent a condition for acceptance of the present, but rather he intended to sell the present except that he erred in the count. In al-Nahr [3/353] he made the corruption in shortage a narration from Abu Hanifa; there is consideration in this, rather it is from some mashayikh and is not correct. (Fath) And he has an option: i.e. the buyer, if he wishes he takes the remainder at its share of the price, and if he wishes he leaves due to the splitting of the transaction. (Miskin, T) It is corrupt: the sale in entirety due to ignorance of the excess leading to dispute. (T)
Source pages p. 256

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling for buying a bundle (adl) of cloths where the number of cloths is specified. The matn states: if someone buys a bundle on the basis that it contains ten cloths, and the actual number is less or more, the sale is corrupt (fasid). However, if the seller specifies a price for each cloth individually and then the count is short, the sale is valid for the existing cloths at their proportionate price, and the buyer has an option (khiyar) due to splitting of the transaction. If the count is excessive, the sale is corrupt because the excess leads to dispute over which cloth is to be returned. The commentary clarifies the reasons: when the total price is given without per-unit pricing, ignorance (jahalah) arises both in the price (if some are missing) and in the identity of the goods (if extra are found). When each cloth is priced, the price for each is known, so the sale is valid for the present cloths and void for the missing ones; the buyer has the option to take or leave. There is a narration from Abu Hanifa that the sale is corrupt even with per-unit pricing because it combines existing and non-existing items in one contract, but the correct (sahih) view according to the later scholars (as stated in al-Nahr) is that it is valid in the case of shortage. The overall ruling: if the total is short and per-unit price is known, the buyer may take the existing goods at their share of the price or cancel; if there is an excess, the sale is entirely corrupt. The authority weight: the primary ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah, with the ijtihad of Abu Hanifa on the per-unit case being outweighed by the consensus of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad and later scholars.

Key Terms
العدل (al-'adl): A bundle or load of cloths; in sales, it is a type of goods that may contain multiple units.
القيمي (al-qimi): Goods that are not measured by weight or volume but have value as individual items (like cloths).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A buyer purchases a bundle of cloths for a total of 30 dirhams, described as 6 cloths. He finds 5 cloths. What is the ruling?
A) The sale is valid, and he pays 25 dirhams.
B) The sale is corrupt; he may return the bundle.
C) The sale is valid, and he pays 30 dirhams.
D) The sale is valid, and he has an option to take 5 or cancel.

Key Takeaway
A bundle sale without per-unit pricing is fasid if the count is off; with per-unit pricing, shortage gives the buyer an option, but excess still invalidates.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Per-Cubit Pricing with Fractional Amounts
Dispute among Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad on options when fractional cubits are found

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rulings of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad on khiyar and price adjustment when the actual measured quantity differs from the specified quantity in a per-unit price sale, and evaluate the practical consequence of each position.

Core Idea
When a sale is priced per cubit, Abu Hanifa treats the cubit as a description; the Sahibayn treat each cubit as an independent unit—leading to different khiyar outcomes.

This passage from al-'Inayah presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute on the legal implications of per-unit pricing. When a cloth is bought at a rate per cubit but the actual length differs, the three imams diverge on whether the buyer has an option (khiyar) and how the price is adjusted. Understanding this dispute clarifies the distinction between 'wasf' and 'asl' in Hanafi sales law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and three positions
Understand the sale: a cloth described as ten cubits at one dirham per cubit. The actual length is either 10.5 (excess) or 9.5 (shortage). For each case, note the ruling of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad regarding the price and the buyer's option.
Abu Hanifa: if excess, pay 10 dirhams, no option; if shortage, pay 9 dirhams, with option. Abu Yusuf: if excess, pay 11 dirhams, with option; if shortage, pay 10 dirhams, with option. Muhammad: if excess, pay 10.5 dirhams, with option; if shortage, pay 9.5 dirhams, with option.
2
Analyze Abu Hanifa's reasoning
Abu Hanifa treats the cubit as a description (wasf) originally, so the named total (ten cubits) is the basis. The excess or shortage is absorbed proportionally, and the option only arises in case of shortage because the transaction is split.
Key principle: 'al-dhira' wasf' – the cubit is a description, not an independent entity.
3
Analyze Abu Yusuf's reasoning
Abu Yusuf treats each cubit as a separate item (like a cloth). Hence, if there is shortage, the price remains fixed (no reduction), and the buyer has an option. If excess, the price increases proportionally and the buyer still has an option.
Each cubit is analogized to an independent unit of sale.
4
Analyze Muhammad's reasoning
Muhammad likens per-cubit pricing to measured goods (mikyal). Therefore, exact proportionality is required: half a cubit corresponds to half a dirham. The buyer has an option in both cases to avoid harm.
Necessity of confronting each unit with its price leads to half-and-half calculation.
5
Compare the practical outcomes
The thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference) is evident in the price and khiyar. Summarize the three outcomes for the excess and shortage cases.
For excess: Abu Hanifa: 10 dirhams, no option; Abu Yusuf: 11 dirhams, option; Muhammad: 10.5 dirhams, option. For shortage: Abu Hanifa: 9 dirhams, option; Abu Yusuf: 10 dirhams, option; Muhammad: 9.5 dirhams, option.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عيني كل ذراع بدرهم فوجده تسعة ونصفا، أو عشرة ونصفا. أخذه بعشرة إلخ: أي من اشترى ثوباً على أنه عشرة أذرع كل ذراع بدرهم، فوجده عشرة ونصفاً، أخذه بعشرة دراهم، ولا خيار له ولو وجده تسعة ونصفاً أخذه بتسعة وله الخيار وهذا عند أبي حنيفة، وقال أبو يوسف يأخذه في الوجه الأول - أي الزيادة - بأحد عشر ، وفي الوجه الثاني بعشرة، ويخير في الوجهين. وقال محمد: يأخذه في الأول بعشرة ونصف، وفي الثاني بتسعة ونصف، ويخير فيهما؛ لأنه لما سمى البائع لكل ذراع ثمنا على حدة التحق كل ذراع بالقدر أي الكيل، ومن ضرورة مقابلة الذراع بالدرهم مقابلة النصف بالنصف، والخيار يثبت له؛ لئلا يتضرر من غير اختيار بزيادة الثمن في الوجه الأول ونقصان المبيع في الوجه الثاني، ولأبي يوسف: أنه لما قابل کل ذراع ،بدرهم صار كل ذراع كثوب على حدة، وقد نقص فلا يسقط شيء من الثمن، ثم يخير؛ = لأنـ.
'Inayah: 'each cubit for a dirham and he found it nine and a half, or ten and a half. He takes it for ten' etc.: meaning whoever bought a cloth on the basis that it is ten cubits, each cubit for a dirham, and he found it ten and a half, he takes it for ten dirhams, and he has no option; and if he found it nine and a half, he takes it for nine and he has an option. And this is according to Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf said: he takes it in the first case - i.e. the increase - for eleven, and in the second case for ten, and he has an option in both cases. And Muhammad said: he takes it in the first for ten and a half, and in the second for nine and a half, and he has an option in both; because when the seller named a price for each cubit separately, each cubit becomes like a measure, i.e. a quantity, and it is necessary from the confrontation of cubit with dirham to confront half with half, and the option is established for him so that he is not harmed involuntarily by the increase of price in the first case and the decrease of the sold item in the second. And for Abu Yusuf: because when he confronted each cubit with a dirham, each cubit became like a cloth separately, and it decreased, so nothing of the price is dropped, then he has an option.
Source pages p. 256

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute (ikhtilaf) from the commentary of al-'Inayah on Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The scenario is a purchase of a cloth described as ten cubits, each cubit for one dirham. The actual length is found to be ten and a half cubits (excess) or nine and a half (shortage). Abu Hanifa rules: if it is ten and a half, the buyer takes it for ten dirhams with no option (the extra half cubit is considered part of the whole at no extra cost because the cubit is a description). If it is nine and a half, the buyer takes it for nine dirhams and has an option (khiyar) due to shortage. Abu Yusuf differs: in the case of excess, the buyer pays for the actual length (eleven dirhams) and has an option; in shortage, he pays the full ten dirhams (no reduction) and has an option. Muhammad's view: in excess, he pays ten and a half; in shortage, he pays nine and a half, and has an option in both cases. The reasoning: Abu Hanifa treats the cubit as a description (wasf) originally, so the named count is like a total description, and the excess or shortage is absorbed with the option at the proportionate price. Abu Yusuf treats each cubit as an individual item (like a cloth), so if there is shortage, the price remains fixed, and if there is excess, the price increases proportionately; the option exists because the buyer did not fully consent to the change. Muhammad makes each cubit analogous to measured goods (mikyal), requiring exact matching of price and quantity, hence the half-and-half calculation. The mufta bihi position: the text does not explicitly state the preferred view, but later Hanafi fatwa tends to side with Abu Hanifa's position as the basis of the school, though in practice the views of the Sahibayn may be applied for justice. The authority weight: this is a Nawadir-type ikhtilaf within the Zahir al-Riwayah, as it involves the foundational rulings of the three major imams.

Key Terms
الذراع وصفاً وأصلاً (al-dhira' wasfan wa aslan): The cubit is considered a description (wasf) by Abu Hanifa, meaning it qualifies the object without being its essence. In contrast, Sahibayn treat each cubit as an independent entity (asl) when priced per unit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if someone buys a cloth described as ten cubits at one dirham per cubit, and finds it to be nine and a half cubits, what is the ruling?
A) The buyer takes it for nine dirhams and has an option.
B) The buyer takes it for ten dirhams and has an option.
C) The sale is corrupt.
D) The buyer takes it for nine and a half dirhams with no option.

Key Takeaway
In per-unit pricing, Abu Hanifa's view that the unit is a description limits the buyer's khiyar in case of excess, while the Sahibayn grant khiyar in both excess and shortage.

Selling Part of a House: Shares vs. Measurements
Ruling on validity of selling specified measurement versus shares in a house

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on selling specified shares versus specified cubits from a house, and apply the principle of eliminating uncertainty to similar sale conditions.

Core Idea
Selling 'shares' is valid; selling 'cubits' is invalid because shares are common portions, but cubits are specific measurements causing uncertainty.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq lays down a fundamental rule in sales (buyu'): the subject matter must be known and free from uncertainty that could lead to dispute. The author contrasts two ways of selling part of a house—by shares versus by specific length—to illustrate how the mode of specification determines validity. A second example reinforces the rule: buying cloth with a condition on quantity that is not met renders the sale void.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two transactions
The passage presents two distinct scenarios: selling a specified number of cubits (10 cubits) from a house without fixing shares, and selling a bundle of cloth with a condition on the number of pieces.
The first scenario is the main ruling; the second is an illustrative furu'.
2
State the ruling for each
For the first: the sale of ten shares (i.e., a specified number of shares) is valid by consensus. The sale of ten cubits without specifying shares is invalid because cubits are specific measurements. For the second: if the bundle does not contain exactly ten pieces, the sale is void.
The ruling for cubits is implicit from the explanation: if shares are valid, cubits are invalid because they create uncertainty.
3
Identify the underlying cause (illah)
The reason for validity of shares is that a 'share' (sahm) is a common, undefined portion; it does not lead to dispute. A 'cubit' (dhira') is a fixed measurement that, when applied to different parts of a house, causes uncertainty about the exact boundaries and thus leads to potential conflict.
The Arabic phrase 'li shuyu' al-sahm la al-dhira'' directly states this.
4
Apply the principle to the cloth example
The cloth transaction involves a condition that the bundle contains ten pieces. If this condition is not met (either less or more), the sale is void because the parties agreed on a specific quantity, and discrepancy creates jahl (ignorance) leading to dispute.
This is a separate ruling but illustrates the same principle: uncertainty about the exact subject matter invalidates the sale.
5
Distinguish from valid partial sales
Selling a specified share (e.g., 1/10) is like selling a percentage, which is clear. Selling a specific area (e.g., 10 square meters) without delineating the exact location or boundaries is invalid because the buyer cannot know what he is getting precisely.
This distinction is key in real estate and co-ownership transactions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عشرة أذرع من دار لا أسهم، أي لا يفسد بيع عشرة أسهم بالإجماع؛ لشيوع السهم لا الذراع. (عيني) ولو اشترى عدلاً على أنه عشرة أثواب فنقص أو زاد فسد.
Ten cubits from a house without shares, meaning: the sale of ten shares is not voided by consensus because the share (sahm) is common, not the cubit. And if one buys a bundle on condition that it is ten pieces and it decreases or increases, the sale is void.
Source pages p. 256

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement. It addresses the sale of a specified number of cubits from a house without specifying shares. The author clarifies that if one sells 'ten shares' (ashum) from a house, the sale is valid by consensus because a share (sahm) is a common portion, whereas a cubit (dhira') is a specific measurement that would lead to uncertainty. The following sentence introduces a separate case: buying a bundle of cloth with a condition that it contains ten pieces, and if that condition is not met (either less or more), the sale is void due to ignorance (jahl) leading to dispute. This is a straightforward statement of the Hanafi ruling.

Key Terms
أسهم (ashum): Shares; plural of sahm, meaning a common fractional part of a whole.
ذراع (dhira'): Cubit; a specific linear measurement. In the context, selling a specific number of cubits from a house without defining shares is invalid.
لا أسهم (la asham): Without shares; i.e., specifying a measurement without a fractional share.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because shares are more valuable.
B) Because shares are common and do not cause dispute.
C) Because the buyer can choose the best part.
D) Because the seller has the right to specify any share.

Key Takeaway
The validity of selling part of a house depends on specifying common shares rather than specific measurements to avoid uncertainty and dispute.

Bundle Sale on Condition of Ten Pieces: Void If Short or Over
Ruling on bundle sale with quantity condition: void if short or over.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a bundle is bought on condition of a specific number of pieces and found deficient or excessive, and explain why the sale is void in both cases.

Core Idea
Ignorance of price or item due to quantity discrepancy voids the sale.

In Hanafi sales law, certainty of essential terms—price and item—is required. When a bundle of cloth is bought on the condition that it contains exactly ten pieces, but it turns out to be less or more, the sale becomes fasid (void). Why? The reason differs between deficiency and excess, but both stem from fatal ignorance that leads to conflict. This lesson unpacks the reasoning from the matn and its commentary.

Guided Path
1
Identify the transaction and condition
The buyer purchases a bundle (ʿidl) on the express condition that it contains ten pieces (athwāb). This condition is a material term of the sale.
2
Analyze the decrease scenario
When the bundle contains fewer than ten pieces, the sale is void because the price per piece becomes unknown. Each piece of cloth is qimi (non-fungible) and cannot be divided proportionally to derive a per-unit price.
Qimi items lack identical units; apportioning a lump sum among them is uncertain.
3
Analyze the increase scenario
When the bundle contains more than ten pieces, the sale is void because the item itself is unknown. The buyer must return the extra piece, but dispute arises over which specific piece to return, leading to conflict (nizāʿ).
Uncertainty about the identity of the returned item invalidates consent.
4
Apply the underlying legal cause (ʿilla)
Both scenarios share the ʿilla of jahl (ignorance) that inevitably leads to dispute. The Hanafi principle holds that any transaction causing or likely causing nizāʿ is invalid.
The prohibition of gharar and jahl ensures contractual stability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو اشترى عدلاً على أنه عشرة أثواب فنقص أو زاد فسد؛ لجهالة الثمن في النقصان؛ لأنه لا ينقسم أجزاؤه على أجزاء القيمي، ولجهالة المبيع في فصل الزيادة؛ لأنه يحتاج إلى رد الزائد، فيتنازعان في الثوب المردود. (فتح)
And if one buys a bundle on condition that it is ten pieces and it decreases or increases, the sale is void due to ignorance of the price in the case of decrease because its parts cannot be divided onto parts of a fungible (qi'mi), and due to ignorance of the item in the case of increase because he needs to return the excess, so they would dispute over the returned piece.
Source pages p. 256

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It elaborates on the previous statement. The author explains that buying a bundle of cloth on condition that it contains ten pieces, but then finding it short or over, the sale is void. The reason for voidness differs: if deficient, the price becomes unknown because each piece's price cannot be determined proportionally when the item is a non-fungible (qimi). If in excess, the item becomes unknown because the buyer must return the extra piece, leading to dispute over which piece is returned. This highlights the Hanafi principle that any transaction leading to dispute (niza') is invalid. The 'illa (effective cause) is the uncertainty that leads to conflict.

Key Terms
القيمي (al-qimi): A non-fungible item; unique items that cannot be replaced by exactly similar units, like cloth.
عدل (ʿidl): A bundle or load of goods, often cloth.
جهالة (jahāla): Ignorance or uncertainty that invalidates a contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the sale void in the case of increase (more than ten pieces)?
A) The price becomes unknown.
B) The item becomes unknown due to dispute over which piece is returned.
C) The seller is enriching himself unfairly.
D) The buyer has no remedy.

Key Takeaway
A sale conditioned on a specific quantity of a non-fungible item is void if the quantity is off, due to fatal uncertainty in price or object.

The Ruling on Buying a Bundle with Per-Piece Price: Deficiency vs Excess
Ruling with proof and intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling to scenarios where a bundle of goods has per-piece pricing but the actual quantity differs from stated, distinguishing between deficiency (valid with option) and excess (void).

Core Idea
Specifying per-piece price cures jahl for the existing items but not for excess quantity.

When purchasing a bundle where each item is priced individually, the legal outcome depends on whether the actual count matches the stated count. This lesson examines the Hanafi position: if less, the sale is valid for what exists with a buyer's option; if more, the sale is void due to uncertainty about the excess. The passage also records an alternative view from Abu Hanifa that the sale is void even in deficiency, but the relied-upon view upholds validity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the transaction structure
Recognize that the buyer and seller agree on a per-piece price for a bundle of identical items (e.g., ten pieces of cloth at one dirham each). The actual count is discovered to be less or more than stated.
The key is that the price per unit is known, but the total quantity is uncertain.
2
Apply the ruling for deficiency
If the bundle contains fewer pieces than stated, the sale is valid (sahih) for the actually present pieces at the agreed per-piece price. The buyer has khiyar (option) to accept or cancel.
Because the price per piece is known, there is no jahl (ignorance) regarding the value of the existing items.
3
Apply the ruling for excess
If the bundle contains more pieces than stated, the sale is void (fasid) entirely. The excess quantity introduces jahl in the price of the additional items, rendering the contract defective.
Even though per-piece price is known, the overall price is uncertain due to the unknown amount of excess.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
Note that a narration from Abu Hanifa declares the sale void in both deficiency and excess because the contract combines existent and non-existent items in one sale. However, the relied-upon view (as recorded in Fath al-Qadir) upholds validity for deficiency, considering that the seller intended to sell the existent items and merely erred in count.
The dispute hinges on whether the intention is to sell the entire lot as a unit or each piece separately.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو بين لكل ثوب ثمناً ونقص صح بقدره وخير، وإن زاد فسد. وفسر بأن قال: بعتك هذا العدل على أنه عشرة أثواب كل ثوب بدرهم. صح بقدر الموجود؛ لأن ثمن كل واحد من الثياب معلوم، فالموجود يصح فيه البيع، ويبطل في المعدوم. وعن أبي حنيفة: أنه يفسد؛ لأن البائع جمع بين معدوم وموجود في صفقة واحدة. والصحيح أنه يجوز في فصل النقصان عندهم جميعاً؛ لأنه لم يجعل قبول العقد في المعدوم شرطاً لقبوله في الموجود، بل قصد بيع الموجود إلا أنه غلط في العدد. (فتح، رمز الحقائق)
And if he specifies the price for each piece and it decreases, it is valid for the amount present and he has an option; and if it increases, it is void. It is interpreted as him saying: I sold you this bundle on condition that it is ten pieces each piece for a dirham. It is valid for what exists because the price of each piece is known, so the sale is valid for the existing ones and void for the missing ones. And from Abu Hanifa: it is void because the seller combined existent and non-existent in one transaction. The correct view is that it is permissible in the case of deficiency according to all of them because he did not make acceptance of the contract on the non-existent a condition for acceptance on the existent, rather he intended to sell the existent but made a mistake in the number.
Source pages p. 256

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with intra-Hanafi dispute. It presents the scenario where a buyer purchases a bundle of cloth with the seller specifying that each piece is priced individually (e.g., ten pieces at one dirham each). If the bundle contains fewer pieces than stated, the sale is valid for the actual pieces present, and the buyer has the option to either take them at the proportional price or cancel. If it contains more, the sale is void entirely due to ignorance of the excess. The text notes a narration from Abu Hanifa that the sale is void even in deficiency because the seller combined existent and non-existent items in one contract. However, the relied-upon view (al-sahih) is that it is valid, as the seller only intended to sell the existent pieces but was mistaken in count. This shows the Hanafi preference for considering the parties' intent over a formal defect.

Key Terms
خير (khiyar): Option to continue or cancel the sale given to the buyer when the goods are deficient relative to the description.
جعل (jahl): Ignorance or uncertainty regarding a material term of the contract, which may render it void.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling when a bundle is bought with per-piece price specified but is found to contain fewer pieces than stated?
A) The sale is void and the buyer must return the goods.
B) The sale is valid for the present pieces, and the buyer has an option to accept or cancel.
C) The sale is valid for the present pieces at the proportional price, and the buyer has no option.
D) The seller must reduce the price to compensate for the shortage, but the sale stands.

Key Takeaway
When per-piece price is specified, deficiency leads to valid sale with option, while excess renders the sale void.
